###### Abstract

This study introduces a new analytical framework for quantifying multivariate risk measures. Using the Wishart process, which is a stochastic process with values in the space of positive definite matrices, we derive several conditional tail risk measures which, thanks to the remarkable analytical properties of the Wishart process, can be explicitly computed up to a one- or two-dimensional integration. These quantities can also be used to solve analytically a capital allocation problem based on conditional moments. Exploiting the stochastic differential equation property of the Wishart process, we show how an intertemporal (i.e., time-lagged) view of these risk measures can be embedded in the proposed framework. Several numerical examples show that the framework is versatile and operational, thus providing a useful tool for risk management.

JEL classification:
  
G11, G12, C46
  
Keywords:
  
Tail conditional expectation, Risk measures, Fourier transform, Wishart process, Portfolio allocation

## 1 Introduction

The modeling of risk measures is crucial for various applications such as risk management and reserving. The literature in this field is extensive and diverse. For example, Landsman and Valdez ([2005](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib33 "Tail conditional expectations for exponential dispersion models")) derive the tail conditional expectation for the exponential dispersion family, Furman and Landsman ([2005](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib41 "Risk capital decomposition for a multivariate dependent gamma portfolio")) examine the tail conditional expectation for a multivariate gamma portfolio with dependent risks, providing explicit formulas for tail conditional expectations and risk capital allocations. Xu and Mao ([2013](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib29 "Optimal capital allocation based on the tail meanâ€“variance model")) solve a capital allocation problem based on a tail mean-variance model that requires the conditional higher moments up to order three of the underlying variables. They illustrate their model using a multivariate elliptical distribution. More recently, Ignatieva and Landsman ([2015](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib26 "Estimating the tails of loss severity via conditional risk measures for the family of symmetric generalised hyperbolic distributions")), Ignatieva and Landsman ([2019](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib42 "Conditional tail risk measures for the skewed generalised hyperbolic family")), and Ignatieva and Landsman ([2021](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib43 "A class of generalised hyper-elliptical distributions and their applications in computing conditional tail risk measures")) compute a closed-form expression for the tail conditional expectation for generalized hyperbolic/hyper-elliptical distributions,  while Ignatieva and Landsman ([2025](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib44 "Tail variance for generalised hyper-elliptical models")) extend these computations to the second order, that is, the tail variance. Cheung et al. ([2022](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib30 "Multivariate matrix-exponential affine mixtures and their applications in risk theory")) compute a wide variety of risk measures for multivariate matrix-exponential affine mixture models.

In this work, we extend the perspective developed in Dufresne et al. ([2009](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib17 "Fourier inversion formulas in option pricing and insurance")), which computes the Tail Conditional Expectation (TCE) for a univariate loss, to a framework that enables the computation of the TCE for risks, whether individual risks or aggregates, of any moment, across a wide range of random variable distributions, provided their moment generating function (MGF) is available.222Whenever the MGF is not available, as in the case of the Pareto distribution, for example, the characteristic function can be used instead; see Dufresne et al. ([2009](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib17 "Fourier inversion formulas in option pricing and insurance")) for the scalar case.

Additionally, our framework incorporates general dependence among risks, or losses across individual lines, by considering distributions on the space of symmetric positive definite matrices, for which the joint MGF is known for many distributions. This approach does not rely on a specific distribution to derive the TCE or any higher order tail conditional moments. If the static distribution used to compute risk measures can be embedded into a (time-dependent) stochastic process, it becomes possible to compute intertemporal or time-lagged TCEs (or any higher order tail conditional moments). The intertemporal/time-lagged TCE represents the expected loss at time t1t\_{1}, given that the loss at time t0t\_{0} exceeded a certain threshold xâˆ—x\_{\*}, where t0<t1t\_{0}<t\_{1}. We can also compute the TCE at two different time points for dependent losses, provided the joint MGF is known at both t0t\_{0} and t1t\_{1} for the individual lines. This property extends the static or time-independent perspective analyzed in the aforementioned literature to the dynamic or time-series point of view considered in more recent studies (e.g., Chavez-Demoulin and Guillou ([2018](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib3 "Extreme quantile estimation for Î²-mixing time series and applications")), Patton et al. ([2019](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib20 "Dynamic semiparametric models for expected shortfall (and value-at-risk)")), Goegebeur and Guillou ([2024](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib5 "A conditional tail expectation type risk measure for time series")), Goegebeur et al. ([2025](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib6 "Marginal expected shortfall risk measure for time series")), or Liu et al. ([2025](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib1 "Time-lagged marginal expected shortfall"))).333The dynamic property can also be understood in the sense of Riedel ([2004](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib39 "Dynamic coherent risk measures")), Artzner et al. ([2007](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib40 "Coherent multiperiod risk adjusted values and Bellmanâ€™s principle")), Hardy and Wirch ([2004](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib8 "The Iterated Cte")), or Devolder and LebÃ¨gue ([2017](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib7 "Iterated VaR or CTE measures: A false good idea?")), which differs from the purely time-series point of view adopted here. Compared to this literature, our modeling strategy based on the Wishart process provides control over both the evolution of losses and their dependencies.

In modeling portfolio losses, it is important to recognize that losses can exhibit dependence across different losses. Traditional copula-based methods often impose constraints on the types of dependencies we can effectively model, limiting their flexibility.  The literature on risk measures using copulas to handle dependence is extensive. Without pretending to be exhaustive, let us mention Cousin and Di Bernardino ([2014](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib15 "On multivariate extensions of conditional-tail-expectation")) and Di Bernardino et al. ([2015](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib16 "On multivariate extensions of the conditional Value-at-Risk measure")).  An alternative to the copula approach is the factor model approach of Furman and Landsman ([2005](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib41 "Risk capital decomposition for a multivariate dependent gamma portfolio")), which is based on a vector of independent positive variables. In this framework, all losses are expressed as linear functions of this vector and share a common component, akin to a principal component analysis. This modeling strategy imposes certain constraints on the sign of the dependencies. The alternative that we propose is to capture these relationships by directly specifying both the losses and their dependence structure simultaneously. A natural framework for this purpose is to view losses within the space of positive definite matrices, similar to how covariances are treated in portfolio theory. This approach not only aligns with the inherent structure of dependence but also allows for richer modeling of the interactions between different losses.

The Wishart process, originally defined by Bru ([1991](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib85 "Wishart processes")), is a flexible process applied in option pricing, mortality modeling, and equity modeling. It is a positive definite matrix process, making it suitable for modeling positive events such as losses and their dependencies.  As such, it can be seen as an extension of Furman and Landsman ([2005](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib41 "Risk capital decomposition for a multivariate dependent gamma portfolio")) where the dependence between the losses is directly modeled. As an affine process, its MGF is known in closed form. Furthermore, the derivative of the MGF can be computed explicitly, a property that plays a crucial role in operationalising the implementation of risk measures. One of the key ingredients of our approach is to express different risk measures in terms of the MGF of the losses, thereby enabling us to fully exploit this property of the Wishart process. Note that many of our results hold for any distribution, as long as its MGF is known. We highlight our framework using the Wishart process, demonstrating that it satisfies the integrability conditions required by our framework and providing a numerical implementation to showcase the speed and accuracy of our results.

The paper is organized as follows. In SectionÂ [2](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S2 "2 The mathematical framework â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."), we introduce the Wishart process and provide its key results, including its MGF and the joint MGF at two different dates. In SectionÂ [3](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3 "3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."), we present our main result: the ability to compute multivariate risk measures using their Fourier transforms. By utilizing the Fourier transform, we express conditional tail expectations in terms of the joint MGF of random variables and derive these expressions even when a temporal element is introduced. We then prove that the Wishart process meets the integrability conditions for applying these results. We show that our approach is comparable to existing frameworks in terms of numerical cost. We also demonstrate how well-known conditional risk measures can be expressed in our framework. In SectionÂ [4](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S4 "4 Numerical experiments â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."), we provide a numerical implementation of the framework on the Wishart process, demonstrating accurate estimates and the effect of dependence on the measures. Finally, we conclude in SectionÂ [5](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S5 "5 Conclusion â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.").

The identity matrix of ğ–¬â€‹(n)\mathsf{M}(n) is denoted InI\_{n}. We also introduce the symbols trâ€‹[â‹…]\textup{tr}[\,\cdot\,] for the trace of a matrix, vecâ€‹(â‹…)\textup{vec}\left(\cdot\right) for the operator which transforms an nÃ—nn\times n matrix into an n2n^{2} vector by stacking the columns, âŠ—\otimes for the Kronecker product, det(â‹…)\det(\cdot) for the determinant of a matrix, and âˆ¥â‹…âˆ¥\|\cdot\| for the matrix norm associated with trâ€‹[â‹…]\textup{tr}[\,\cdot\,].

The Wishart process was initially defined and analyzed in Bru ([1991](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib85 "Wishart processes")) under the assumption that Ï‰=Î²â€‹Ïƒ2\omega=\beta\sigma^{2} with Î²âˆˆâ„+\beta\in\mathbb{R}\_{+} such that Î²â‰¥n+1\beta\geq n+1 to ensure that for all t>0t>0 we have xtâˆˆğ•Šn++x\_{t}\in\mathbb{S}\_{n}^{++}. Hereafter, this specification will be referred to as the Bru case. It was later extended in Mayerhofer et al. ([2011](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib89 "On strong solutions of positive definite jump-diffusions")) (see also Cuchiero et al. ([2011](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib88 "Affine processes on positive semidefinite matrices"))) to the case Ï‰âˆˆğ•Šn++\omega\in\mathbb{S}\_{n}^{++} and proved that if

|  | Ï‰âª°Î²â€‹Ïƒ2,\displaystyle\omega\succeq\beta\sigma^{2}\,, |  | (2) |

with Î²â‰¥n+1\beta\geq n+1, where ([2](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S2.E2 "In 2 The mathematical framework â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. The infinitesimal generator of the Wishart process is given by Bru ([1991](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib85 "Wishart processes")):

|  |  |  |  |

Bru ([1991](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib85 "Wishart processes")) showed that as the Wishart process is affine, its MGF is exponentially affine. More precisely, the MGF of xtx\_{t} is given by the following proposition, see Grasselli and Tebaldi ([2008](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib86 "Solvable affine term structure models")) and Alfonsi ([2015](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib37 "Affine diffusions and related processes: simulation, theory and applications")) for details.

###### Corollary 2.2.

If we assume that Ï‰=Î²â€‹Ïƒ2\omega=\beta\sigma^{2} with Î²âˆˆâ„\beta\in\mathbb{R} and Î²â‰¥n+1\beta\geq n+1, then the MGF of xâˆ=limtâ†’+âˆxtx\_{\infty}=\lim\_{t\to+\infty}x\_{t}, denoted Î¦âˆâ€‹(Î¸):=limtâ†’+âˆÎ¦â€‹(t,Î¸,x0)=ğ”¼â€‹[etrâ€‹[Î¸â€‹xâˆ]]\Phi^{\infty}(\theta):=\lim\_{t\to+\infty}\Phi(t,\theta,x\_{0})=\mathbb{E}\left[e^{\textup{tr}[\theta x\_{\infty}]}\right], is given for Î¸âˆˆğ•Šn\theta\in\mathbb{S}\_{n} by

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Î¦âˆâ€‹(Î¸)=1det(Inâˆ’2â€‹Ï‚âˆâ€‹Î¸)Î²/2,\displaystyle\Phi^{\infty}(\theta)=\frac{1}{\det(I\_{n}-2\varsigma\_{\infty}\theta)^{\beta/2}}, |  | (10) |

with Ï‚âˆ=limtâ†’+âˆÏ‚t\varsigma\_{\infty}=\lim\_{t\to+\infty}\varsigma\_{t} that is well-defined.

Note that ([10](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S2.E10 "In Corollary 2.2. â€£ 2 The mathematical framework â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) is the MGF of a matrix gamma distribution, and for diagonal parameters, the vector (x11,âˆ,â€¦,xnâ€‹n,âˆ)(x\_{11,\infty},\ldots,x\_{nn,\infty}) is an nn-dimensional vector of independent scalar gamma variables such that xiâ€‹i,âˆx\_{ii,\infty} has a scale 2â€‹(Ï‚âˆ)â€‹iâ€‹i2(\varsigma\_{\infty}){ii} and shape Î²/2\beta/2. This type of distribution is used in Furman and Landsman ([2005](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib41 "Risk capital decomposition for a multivariate dependent gamma portfolio")) to analyse the TCE risk measure.  Since the components of the vector are independent, the authors express the losses as linear functions of this vector, with the dependence between losses captured by a common component of the vector gamma distribution. This common-factor perspective imposes a sign constraint on the dependencies between losses. Note that in the non-diagonal case, the components xiâ€‹i,âˆx\_{ii,\infty} are dependent, and therefore it provides an alternative modeling strategy to create dependence compared to the one used in Furman and Landsman ([2005](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib41 "Risk capital decomposition for a multivariate dependent gamma portfolio")), which consists of specifying a common factor.

To compute the conditional risk measures, we will need the derivative of the MGF with respect to a scalar parameter that multiplies its matrix argument. This relies on Lax ([2007](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib48 "Linear algebra and its applications"), Theorem 4, p. 127) and Lax ([2007](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib48 "Linear algebra and its applications"), Theorem 2, p. 124).

###### Proposition 2.3.

Given a Wishart process (xt)tâ‰¥0(x\_{t})\_{t\geq 0} and for Ïµ>0\epsilon>0 let Î½âˆˆâ„\nu\in\mathbb{R} with Î½âˆˆ]âˆ’Ïµ,Ïµ[\nu\in]-\epsilon,\;\epsilon[. Assume that Î¸0,Î¸1âˆˆğ•Šn\theta\_{0},\theta\_{1}\in\mathbb{S}\_{n} (that do not depend on Î½\nu), and define the MGF

| --- | --- | --- | --- |

|  |  | =Î¦â€‹(t,Î¸0+Î½â€‹Î¸1,x0),\displaystyle=\Phi(t,\theta\_{0}+\nu\theta\_{1},x\_{0})\,, |  | (11) |

with Î¦(.,.,.)\Phi(.,.,.) given by ([5](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S2.E5 "In Proposition 2.1. â€£ 2 The mathematical framework â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. with

while bÎ½â€‹(t,Î¸0,Î¸1)=âˆ«0tğ—ğ—‹â€‹[Ï‰â€‹aÎ½â€‹(u,Î¸0,Î¸1)]â€‹ğ‘‘ub\_{\nu}(t,\theta\_{0},\theta\_{1})=\int\_{0}^{t}\mathsf{tr}[\omega a\_{\nu}(u,\theta\_{0},\theta\_{1})]du.

If we further assume that Ï‰=Î²â€‹Ïƒ2\omega=\beta\sigma^{2} with Î²âˆˆâ„\beta\in\mathbb{R} and Î²â‰¥n+1\beta\geq n+1 then bÎ½â€‹(t,Î¸0,Î¸1)=Î²â€‹trâ€‹[(Inâˆ’2â€‹Ï‚tâ€‹Î¸0)âˆ’1â€‹Ï‚tâ€‹Î¸1]b\_{\nu}(t,\theta\_{0},\theta\_{1})=\beta\textup{tr}[(I\_{n}-2\varsigma\_{t}\theta\_{0})^{-1}\varsigma\_{t}\theta\_{1}].

Note that for Î¦Â¯â€‹(t,Î½,Î¸0,Î¸1,x0)\bar{\Phi}(t,\nu,\theta\_{0},\theta\_{1},x\_{0}) to be well-defined, the norm of Î¸0+Î½â€‹Î¸1\theta\_{0}+\nu\theta\_{1} needs to be sufficiently small. If Ïµ\epsilon is sufficiently small and the norm of Î¸0\theta\_{0} is also sufficiently small, then the function is well-defined according to PropositionÂ [2.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S2.Thmtheorem1 "Proposition 2.1. â€£ 2 The mathematical framework â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."). Note also that if the norm of Î¸0\theta\_{0} is sufficiently small, then (Inâˆ’2â€‹Î¸0â€‹Ï‚t)(I\_{n}-2\theta\_{0}\varsigma\_{t}) is invertible since Ï‚tâˆˆğ•Šn++\varsigma\_{t}\in\mathbb{S}\_{n}^{++}.

The above proposition gives the first order derivative of the moment generating function with respect to Î½\nu. Below, we will need the qâ€‹-thq\text{-th} order derivative, where qâˆˆâ„•q\in\mathbb{N}, of this function with respect to this parameter.

###### Corollary 2.4.

Assume that Ï‰=Î²â€‹Ïƒ2\omega=\beta\sigma^{2} with Î²âˆˆâ„\beta\in\mathbb{R} and Î²â‰¥n+1\beta\geq n+1 and let Î¦Â¯(.,.,.,.)\bar{\Phi}(.,.,.,.) be given by ([11](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S2.E11 "In Proposition 2.3. â€£ 2 The mathematical framework â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")). Then the qâ€‹-thq\text{-th} order derivative of Î¦Â¯â€‹(t,Î½,Î¸0,Î¸1,x0)\bar{\Phi}(t,\nu,\theta\_{0},\theta\_{1},x\_{0}) with respect to Î½\nu (evaluated for Î½=0\nu=0) is given by

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Î¦Â¯Î½qâ€‹(t,Î¸0,Î¸1,x0)\displaystyle\bar{\Phi}\_{\nu^{q}}(t,\theta\_{0},\theta\_{1},x\_{0}) | :=âˆ‚qÎ¦Â¯â€‹(t,Î½,Î¸0,Î¸1,x0)âˆ‚Î½q|Î½=0.\displaystyle:=\left.\frac{\partial^{q}\bar{\Phi}(t,\nu,\theta\_{0},\theta\_{1},x\_{0})}{\partial\nu^{q}}\right|\_{\nu=0}. |  | (14) |

The previous results can be extended to the MGF of the process at two different times thanks to the affine property of the Wishart process. Indeed, in addition to the MGF of the Wishart process at a given point in time, i.e., the marginal point of the process, it is of practical interest to consider two points in time 0<t0<t10<t\_{0}<t\_{1} and the MGF of (xt0,xt1)(x\_{t\_{0}},x\_{t\_{1}}). This will allow us to consider losses at two different dates, thus introducing an intertemporal  or time-lagged perspective to the risk measurement problem. It is easy to obtain the following result from PropositionÂ [2.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S2.Thmtheorem1 "Proposition 2.1. â€£ 2 The mathematical framework â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.") and the use of the law of iterated expectation.

###### Proposition 2.5.

Let (xt)tâ‰¥0(x\_{t})\_{t\geq 0} a Wishart process given by Â ([1](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S2.E1 "In 2 The mathematical framework â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Î¦â€‹(t0,t1,Î¸0,Î¸1,x0)\displaystyle\Phi(t\_{0},t\_{1},\theta\_{0},\theta\_{1},x\_{0}) | :=ğ”¼â€‹[expâ¡(trâ€‹[Î¸0â€‹xt0]+trâ€‹[Î¸1â€‹xt1])]\displaystyle:=\mathbb{E}\left[\exp\left(\textup{tr}[\theta\_{0}x\_{t\_{0}}]+\textup{tr}[\theta\_{1}x\_{t\_{1}}]\right)\right] |  |

where Î¸0\theta\_{0} and Î¸1\theta\_{1} belong to ğ•Šn\mathbb{S}\_{n}, a(.,.)a(.,.) and b(.,.)b(.,.) are given by PropositionÂ [2.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S2.Thmtheorem1 "Proposition 2.1. â€£ 2 The mathematical framework â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. ###### Proof.

Using the law of iterated expectation, we have

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Î¦â€‹(t0,t1,Î¸0,Î¸1,x0)\displaystyle\Phi(t\_{0},t\_{1},\theta\_{0},\theta\_{1},x\_{0}) | =ğ”¼â€‹[expâ¡(trâ€‹[Î¸0â€‹xt0]+trâ€‹[Î¸1â€‹xt1])]\displaystyle=\mathbb{E}\left[\exp\left(\textup{tr}[\theta\_{0}x\_{t\_{0}}]+\textup{tr}[\theta\_{1}x\_{t\_{1}}]\right)\right] |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | =ğ”¼â€‹[ğ”¼â€‹[expâ¡(trâ€‹[Î¸0â€‹xt0]+trâ€‹[Î¸1â€‹xt1])|â„±t0]]\displaystyle=\mathbb{E}\big[\mathbb{E}[\exp\left(\textup{tr}[\theta\_{0}x\_{t\_{0}}]+\textup{tr}[\theta\_{1}x\_{t\_{1}}]\right)|\mathcal{F}\_{t\_{0}}]\big] |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | =ğ”¼â€‹[expâ¡(trâ€‹(Î¸0â€‹xt0))â‹…expâ¡(trâ€‹[aâ€‹(t1âˆ’t0,Î¸1)â€‹xt0]+bâ€‹(t1âˆ’t0,Î¸1))]\displaystyle=\mathbb{E}\left[\exp\left(\textup{tr}(\theta\_{0}x\_{t\_{0}})\right)\cdot\exp(\textup{tr}[a(t\_{1}-t\_{0},\theta\_{1})x\_{t\_{0}}]+b(t\_{1}-t\_{0},\theta\_{1}))\right] |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | =expâ¡(trâ€‹[aâ€‹(t0,Î¸0+aâ€‹(t1âˆ’t0,Î¸1))â€‹x0]+bâ€‹(t0,Î¸0)+bâ€‹(t1âˆ’t0,Î¸1)).\displaystyle=\exp\left(\textup{tr}[a(t\_{0},\theta\_{0}+a(t\_{1}-t\_{0},\theta\_{1}))x\_{0}]+b(t\_{0},\theta\_{0})+b(t\_{1}-t\_{0},\theta\_{1})\right). |  |

âˆ

A natural extension of PropositionÂ [2.5](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S2.Thmtheorem5 "Proposition 2.5. â€£ 2 The mathematical framework â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. ###### Proposition 2.6.

We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")). These functions can be explicitly computed.

This derivative also involves the functions âˆ‚Î½0bâ€‹(t1âˆ’t0,Î½0â€‹Î¸0+Î½1â€‹Î¸1)\partial\_{\nu\_{0}}b(t\_{1}-t\_{0},\nu\_{0}\theta\_{0}+\nu\_{1}\theta\_{1}), âˆ‚Î½1bâ€‹(t1âˆ’t0,Î½0â€‹Î¸0+Î½1â€‹Î¸1)\partial\_{\nu\_{1}}b(t\_{1}-t\_{0},\nu\_{0}\theta\_{0}+\nu\_{1}\theta\_{1}) and âˆ‚Î½0â€‹Î½12bâ€‹(t1âˆ’t0,Î½0â€‹Î¸0+Î½1â€‹Î¸1)\partial\_{\nu\_{0}\nu\_{1}}^{2}b(t\_{1}-t\_{0},\nu\_{0}\theta\_{0}+\nu\_{1}\theta\_{1}). If we further assume that Ï‰=Î²â€‹Ïƒ2\omega=\beta\sigma^{2} with Î²âˆˆâ„\beta\in\mathbb{R} and Î²â‰¥n+1\beta\geq n+1 then they are equal for Î½0=0\nu\_{0}=0 and Î½1=0\nu\_{1}=0 to Î²2â€‹trâ€‹[2â€‹Ï‚t1âˆ’t0â€‹Î¸0]\frac{\beta}{2}\textup{tr}[2\varsigma\_{t\_{1}-t\_{0}}\theta\_{0}], Î²2â€‹trâ€‹[2â€‹Ï‚t1âˆ’t0â€‹Î¸1]\frac{\beta}{2}\textup{tr}[2\varsigma\_{t\_{1}-t\_{0}}\theta\_{1}] and 2â€‹Î²â€‹trâ€‹[Ï‚t1âˆ’t0â€‹Î¸1â€‹Ï‚t1âˆ’t0â€‹Î¸0]2\beta\textup{tr}[\varsigma\_{t\_{1}-t\_{0}}\theta\_{1}\varsigma\_{t\_{1}-t\_{0}}\theta\_{0}], respectively.

The previous derivative function can be extended to a higher order by performing additional derivations. The following corollary is more for notational purposes.

###### Corollary 2.7.

Assume that Ï‰=Î²â€‹Ïƒ2\omega=\beta\sigma^{2} with Î²âˆˆâ„\beta\in\mathbb{R} and Î²â‰¥n+1\beta\geq n+1 and let Î¦~(.,.,.,.)\tilde{\Phi}(.,.,.,.) be given by ([16](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S2.E16 "In Proposition 2.6. â€£ 2 The mathematical framework â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")). Then the (pâ€‹-th,qâ€‹-th)(p\text{-th},q\text{-th}) order derivative, with (p,q)âˆˆâ„•2(p,q)\in\mathbb{N}^{2}, of Î¦~â€‹(t0,t1,Î¸Â¯0,Î½0,Î½1,Î¸0,Î¸1,x0)\tilde{\Phi}(t\_{0},t\_{1},\bar{\theta}\_{0},\nu\_{0},\nu\_{1},\theta\_{0},\theta\_{1},x\_{0}) with respect to (Î½0,Î½1)(\nu\_{0},\nu\_{1}) (evaluated for Î½0=0\nu\_{0}=0 and Î½1=0\nu\_{1}=0) is

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Î¦~Î½0pâ€‹Î½1qâ€‹(t0,t1,Î¸Â¯0,Î¸0,Î¸1,x0)\displaystyle\tilde{\Phi}\_{\nu\_{0}^{p}\nu\_{1}^{q}}(t\_{0},t\_{1},\bar{\theta}\_{0},\theta\_{0},\theta\_{1},x\_{0}) | :=âˆ‚p+qÎ¦~â€‹(t0,t1,Î¸Â¯0,Î½0,Î½1,Î¸0,Î¸1,x0)âˆ‚Î½0pâ€‹âˆ‚Î½1q|Î½0=0,Î½1=0.\displaystyle:=\left.\frac{\partial^{p+q}\tilde{\Phi}(t\_{0},t\_{1},\bar{\theta}\_{0},\nu\_{0},\nu\_{1},\theta\_{0},\theta\_{1},x\_{0})}{\partial\nu\_{0}^{p}\partial\nu\_{1}^{q}}\right|\_{\nu\_{0}=0,\nu\_{1}=0}. |  | (18) |

## 3 Conditional tail risk measures

In this section, we begin by reformulating the key quantities required to compute conditional higher moments in terms of their Fourier transform representations, as outlined in SectionÂ [3.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.SS1 "3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."). While these Fourier transform representations of the tail conditional expectations may seem standard, to the best of our knowledge, they have not been previously reported in the literature in the multivariate and/or the higher order moments cases.444A Fourier transform representation of the TCE\operatorname{TCE} in the univariate case appears in Dufresne et al. ([2009](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib17 "Fourier inversion formulas in option pricing and insurance")). Even if they are of interest, these Fourier transform representations involve multidimensional integrations that are numerically demanding. As such, they do not provide an interesting alternative to conditional higher moments computed using the density of the state variable, which is the standard approach used in the literature. To overcome this difficulty, in SectionÂ [3.2](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.SS2 "3.2 One-dimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.") we introduce one-dimensional Fourier transform representations for these risk measures, thereby significantly reducing the computational cost. However, this comes at the cost of computing the (higher) derivative of the MGF of the Wishart process, but this can be done as shown in the previous section. Note that these results apply not only to the Wishart process, but to any distribution with a known MGF,555Throughout, we treat the MGF as a function of a complex parameter and work on the domain where it is finite. On the imaginary axis z=iâ€‹vz=\mathrm{i}v this coincides with the characteristic function Ï†Yâ€‹(v)=ğ”¼â€‹[eiâ€‹vâ€‹Y]\varphi\_{Y}(v)=\mathbb{E}\!\left[e^{\mathrm{i}vY}\right], which always exists. Unless stated otherwise, â€œMGFâ€ refers to this complex-argument version. so these results have broad applicability that goes well beyond the particular case of the Wishart process that we use here. We begin by presenting the Fourier transform representations of the risk measures in a very general way in SectionÂ [3.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.SS1 "3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.") and SectionÂ [3.2](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.SS2 "3.2 One-dimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."), and then illustrate them in the particular case of the Wishart process in SectionÂ [3.3](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.SS3 "3.3 Wishart conditional tail risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."). We end this section by providing a comparison, in terms of computational cost, of our approach with the standard strategy used in the literature.

### 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures

When considering only one loss or a scalar loss, then the standard risk measures are the higher moments conditional on the loss being above a certain threshold. By Bayesâ€™ theorem we have the following expression for the moment of a variable YY conditional on the fact that this variable is above a certain threshold:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ğ”¼â€‹[Ypâ€‹|Y>â€‹yâˆ—]=ğ”¼â€‹[Ypâ€‹ğŸ{Y>yâˆ—}]ğ”¼â€‹[ğŸ{Y>yâˆ—}],\displaystyle\mathbb{E}[Y^{p}|Y>y\_{\*}]=\frac{\mathbb{E}[Y^{p}\mathbf{1}\_{\{Y>y\_{\*}\}}]}{\mathbb{E}[\mathbf{1}\_{\{Y>y\_{\*}\}}]}, |  | (19) |

which for p=1p=1 is commonly denoted in the literature as TCEYâ¡(yâˆ—)\operatorname{TCE}\_{Y}(y\_{\*}) and is the tail conditional expectation. Thus, the evaluation of ([19](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E19 "In 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) amounts to the calculation of ğ”¼â€‹[Ypâ€‹ğŸ{Y>yâˆ—}]\mathbb{E}[Y^{p}\mathbf{1}\_{\{Y>y\_{\*}\}}], which is commonly done using the density of the variable YY. We reformulate this expectation in terms of the MGF of this variable, thus avoiding the use of its density. The proposition below shows how to calculate this.

###### Proposition 3.1.

Denote YY a positive (scalar) random variable and denote by Î¦Yâ€‹(v)=ğ”¼â€‹[evâ€‹Y]\Phi\_{Y}(v)=\mathbb{E}\left[e^{vY}\right] for vâˆˆâ„v\in\mathbb{R} its MGF. Let yâˆ—âˆˆâ„+y\_{\*}\in\mathbb{R}\_{+}, Î±1âˆˆâ„+\alpha\_{1}\in\mathbb{R}\_{+} and assume u1âˆˆâ„â†’Î¦Yâ€‹(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)j+1u\_{1}\in\mathbb{R}\to\frac{\Phi\_{Y}(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})}{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})^{j+1}} (with i=âˆ’1\mathrm{i}=\sqrt{-1}) is integrable for j=0,â€¦,pj=0,\ldots,p with pâˆˆâ„•p\in\mathbb{N}. Then

with cj=Î“â€‹(j+1)c\_{j}=\Gamma(j+1) and Î“(.)\Gamma(.) the gamma function.

that leads to the result after considering the real part of the right hand side of the above equation since the left hand side is real. âˆ

Note that the result applies to distributions defined not only on â„+\mathbb{R}\_{+}, but also on â„\mathbb{R}, provided the integrability condition is satisfied, and if we opted to use the characteristic function Ï†Yâ€‹(v)=ğ”¼â€‹[eiâ€‹vâ€‹Y]\varphi\_{Y}(v)=\mathbb{E}\left[e^{\mathrm{i}vY}\right] (which always exists for real vv) instead of the MGF Î¦Yâ€‹(v)=ğ”¼â€‹[evâ€‹Y]\Phi\_{Y}(v)=\mathbb{E}\left[e^{vY}\right], it would amount to changing Î¦Yâ€‹(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)\Phi\_{Y}(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1}) in ([20](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E20 "In Proposition 3.1. â€£ 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) to Ï†Yâ€‹(âˆ’iâ€‹Î±1âˆ’u1)\varphi\_{Y}(-\mathrm{i}\alpha\_{1}-u\_{1}). The proof remains unchanged. Since we use the MGF of the Wishart process (see, for example, Grasselli and Tebaldi ([2008](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib86 "Solvable affine term structure models")) and Alfonsi ([2015](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib37 "Affine diffusions and related processes: simulation, theory and applications"))), we formulate our results in terms of the MGF instead of the characteristic function. However, we stress that all results of this work can easily accommodate the characteristic function instead.

The above result already illustrates the advantage of using a Fourier representation of risk measures, since the above result applies for any pâ€‹-thp\text{-th} moment and any distribution with known MGF. But the result is far more interesting when considering the multivariate case. Indeed, if (Y1,â‹¯,Yn)(Y\_{1},\cdots,Y\_{n}) is a vector of losses and S=âˆ‘i=1nYiS=\sum\_{i=1}^{n}Y\_{i} is the sum of losses, only under very special loss distributions will the density of SS be known in closed form, whereas the MGF Î¦(Y1,â‹¯,Yn)â€‹(z1,â‹¯,zn)\Phi\_{(Y\_{1},\cdots,Y\_{n})}(z\_{1},\cdots,z\_{n}) of (Y1,â‹¯,Yn)(Y\_{1},\cdots,Y\_{n}) may be known, so that the MGF of SS is then known since Î¦Sâ€‹(z)=Î¦(Y1,â‹¯,Yn)â€‹(z,â‹¯,z)\Phi\_{S}(z)=\Phi\_{(Y\_{1},\cdots,Y\_{n})}(z,\cdots,z), and the aforementioned risk measures can be computed up to a one-dimensional integration.666If (Y1,â‹¯,Yn)(Y\_{1},\cdots,Y\_{n}) is a random vector with a known density, only for certain specific distributions the density of the sum S=âˆ‘1nYiS=\sum\_{1}^{n}Y\_{i} is known in closed form (it is the convolution). Further to this, in the multivariate case it is relevant to compute the moment of a product of given losses conditional on one of the loss, often the sum of the losses but it does not have to be the sum, being above a certain threshold. Proceeding as for ([19](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E19 "In 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")), the problem amounts to calculate

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ğ”¼â€‹[Zqâ€‹Ypâ€‹|Y>â€‹yâˆ—]=ğ”¼â€‹[Zqâ€‹Ypâ€‹ğŸ{Y>yâˆ—}]ğ”¼â€‹[ğŸ{Y>yâˆ—}],\displaystyle\mathbb{E}[Z^{q}Y^{p}|Y>y\_{\*}]=\frac{\mathbb{E}[Z^{q}Y^{p}\mathbf{1}\_{\{Y>y\_{\*}\}}]}{\mathbb{E}[\mathbf{1}\_{\{Y>y\_{\*}\}}]}, |  | (23) |

where ZZ is one element of (Y1,â€¦,Yn)(Y\_{1},\ldots,Y\_{n}) or a linear combination of the elements of (Y1,â€¦,Yn)(Y\_{1},\ldots,Y\_{n}) and therefore to determine the numerator of the above equation. Note that in ([23](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E23 "In 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")), YY can be either an individual loss, i.e., YiY\_{i} for i=1,â‹¯,ni=1,\cdots,n, or a sum of losses S=âˆ‘i=1nYiS=\sum\_{i=1}^{n}Y\_{i}. It is presented in the following proposition.

###### Proposition 3.2.

Let (Y,Z)âˆˆâ„+2(Y,Z)\in\mathbb{R}\_{+}^{2} a 2-dimensional random vector and denote by Î¦(Y,Z)â€‹(v1,v2)=ğ”¼â€‹[ev1â€‹Y+v2â€‹Z]\Phi\_{(Y,Z)}(v\_{1},v\_{2})=\mathbb{E}[e^{v\_{1}Y+v\_{2}Z}] for (v1,v2)âˆˆâ„2(v\_{1},v\_{2})\in\mathbb{R}^{2} its MGF. Let yâˆ—âˆˆâ„+y\_{\*}\in\mathbb{R}\_{+}, (Î±1,Î±2)âˆˆâ„+2(\alpha\_{1},\alpha\_{2})\in\mathbb{R}\_{+}^{2}. Assume suitable integrability conditions of the functions (u1,u2)âˆˆâ„2â†’Î¦(Y,Z)â€‹(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1,Î±2âˆ’iâ€‹u2)(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)j+1â€‹(Î±2âˆ’iâ€‹u2)p+1(u\_{1},u\_{2})\in\mathbb{R}^{2}\to\frac{\Phi\_{(Y,Z)}(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1},\alpha\_{2}-\mathrm{i}u\_{2})}{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})^{j+1}(\alpha\_{2}-\mathrm{i}u\_{2})^{p+1}} for j=0,â€¦,pj=0,\ldots,p. Then

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |

Note that the previous two results apply to distributions defined not only on â„+2\mathbb{R}\_{+}^{2}, but also on â„2\mathbb{R}^{2}, provided the integrability conditions are satisfied and the following a minor adjustment to the proof is added. If ZZ has a distribution defined on â„\mathbb{R}, then writing z=(z)+âˆ’(âˆ’z)+z=(z)\_{+}-(-z)\_{+} so that zq=(z)+qâˆ’(âˆ’z)+qz^{q}=(z)\_{+}^{q}-(-z)\_{+}^{q}, the first term is handled using Bateman and ErdÃ©lyi ([1954](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib46 "Tables of integral transforms"), 3.2(3)) while the second term is handled using Bateman and ErdÃ©lyi ([1954](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib46 "Tables of integral transforms"), 3.2(4)).

###### Remark 3.3.

Underlying ([20](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E20 "In Proposition 3.1. â€£ 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) and ([24](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E24 "In Proposition 3.2. â€£ 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) is the Plancherel-Parseval equality which states that the integral of the product of two functions is equal, up to a scaling parameter, to the integral of the product of the Fourier (or Laplace, Mellin) transform of these functions, see DLMF ([2010](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib45 "Digital library of mathematical functions"), Section 1.14). This equality is of practical importance since if the integral represents an expectation of a given function of a random variable, then this expectation can be expressed as the product of the function of the random variable and the density of this random variable. The Plancherel-Parseval equality implies that this expectation is given by the integral of the Fourier transform of the density, which is the characteristic function of the random variable, and the Fourier transform of the given function. If the density of the random variable is known, then the expectation can be computed using the density, and there is no need to rely on this Fourier representation. However, it can become quickly tedious. For example, Ignatieva and Landsman ([2021](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib43 "A class of generalised hyper-elliptical distributions and their applications in computing conditional tail risk measures")) compute the TCE for a class of generalized hyper-elliptical distributions, while in Ignatieva and Landsman ([2025](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib44 "Tail variance for generalised hyper-elliptical models")) they extend the computations to the second moment, that is, the tail variance. Higher order (conditional) moments have yet to be determined. If the density of the random variable is unknown (or challenging to compute numerically) but its MGF is known, there are two alternatives. The first consists in computing the density using the inverse
Fourier transform of the characteristic function and then to integrate (numerically) the density. This is done in Nguyen and Nguyen ([2017](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib9 "Risk measures computation by Fourier inversion")) or Blier-Wong et al. ([2025](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib10 "Efficient evaluation of risk allocations")). Although it is a possible route, ([20](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E20 "In Proposition 3.1. â€£ 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) and ([24](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E24 "In Proposition 3.2. â€£ 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) suggest a better alternative solution, which consists in using the Plancherel-Parseval and integrate the product. To this end, one needs to compute the Fourier transform of function involved in the risk measure. For the TCE, this computation is well-known since it is standard in the option pricing literature, and not surprisingly, in Dufresne et al. ([2009](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib17 "Fourier inversion formulas in option pricing and insurance")), Bormetti et al. ([2010](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib11 "A generalized Fourier transform approach to risk measures")) or KÃ©lani and Quittard-Pinon ([2014](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib12 "Pricing, hedging and assessing risk in a general LÃ©vy context")), this link to this literature is explicitly underlined. As a result, our work extends the literature in two ways. First, we consider higher (conditional) moments as ([20](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E20 "In Proposition 3.1. â€£ 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) clearly shows. Second, we consider the multivariate case in ([24](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E24 "In Proposition 3.2. â€£ 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")). Note that this result applies to variables with a general distribution, particularly when these variables are the sum of other random variables, as is typical when considering a portfolio. In such situations, a computational approach based on the density can be problematic. Also, multidimensional problem often come with computational difficulties that we partially solve. We elaborate further on this point in the next section.

The above result requires a 2-dimensional integration, and if we consider more variables, but still conditioning on one of them, it will lead to a multi-dimensional Fourier transform (of dimension equal to the number of variables considered), and therefore to a numerical difficulty similar to that encountered when working with the density of a state variable used for the losses. The next section shows how this numerical difficulty can be replaced by a one-dimensional integration and derivation of a function that is related to the derivative of the MGF of the state variable. The difference is important since we have seen in the analytical section that the MGF of the Wishart process is easy to derive.

### 3.2 One-dimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures

In this section, we reformulate Proposition [3.2](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem2 "Proposition 3.2. â€£ 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.") in a more efficient way from a numerical point of view. Essentially, it requires to be able to compute the derivative of the MGF of the state variable which can typically be done analytically.

###### Proposition 3.4.

Let (Y,Z)âˆˆâ„+2(Y,Z)\in\mathbb{R}\_{+}^{2} the 2-dimensional vector of proposition [3.2](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem2 "Proposition 3.2. â€£ 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.") and Î¦(Y,Z)â€‹(v1,v2)\Phi\_{(Y,Z)}(v\_{1},v\_{2}) its MGF of (Y,Z)(Y,Z). Denote by Î¦(Y,Z)(0,q)â€‹(v1,v2)\Phi\_{(Y,Z)}^{(0,q)}(v\_{1},v\_{2}) for (v1,v2)âˆˆâ„2(v\_{1},v\_{2})\in\mathbb{R}^{2} its qâ€‹-thq\text{-th} order derivative, where qâˆˆâ„q\in\mathbb{R}, with respect to v2v\_{2} (and 0â€‹-th0\text{-th} order derivative with respect to v1v\_{1}). Let yâˆ—âˆˆâ„+y\_{\*}\in\mathbb{R}\_{+}, Î±1âˆˆâ„+\alpha\_{1}\in\mathbb{R}\_{+} and assume suitable integrability conditions of the functions u1âˆˆâ„â†’Î¦(Y,Z)(0,q)â€‹(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1,0)(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)j+1u\_{1}\in\mathbb{R}\to\frac{\Phi\_{(Y,Z)}^{(0,q)}(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1},0)}{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})^{j+1}} for j=0,â€¦,pj=0,\ldots,p. Then the following relation holds

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ğ”¼â€‹[Zqâ€‹Ypâ€‹ğŸ{Y>yâˆ—}]=âˆ«0+âˆâˆ‘j=0p(pj)â€‹yâˆ—pâˆ’jâ€‹Î“â€‹(j+1)Ï€â€‹â„œâ¡(eâˆ’(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)â€‹yâˆ—â€‹Î¦(Y,Z)(0,q)â€‹(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1,0)(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)j+1)â€‹dâ€‹u1.\displaystyle\mathbb{E}[Z^{q}Y^{p}\mathbf{1}\_{\{Y>y\_{\*}\}}]=\int\_{0}^{+\infty}\sum\_{j=0}^{p}\binom{p}{j}\frac{y\_{\*}^{p-j}\Gamma(j+1)}{\pi}\Re\left(\frac{e^{-(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})y\_{\*}}\Phi\_{(Y,Z)}^{(0,q)}(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1},0)}{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})^{j+1}}\right)du\_{1}. |  | (25) |

###### Proof.

Proceeding as in the previous proof but not using a Fourier transform for the variable ZZ, we can reach

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ğ”¼â€‹[Zqâ€‹(Yâˆ’yâˆ—)+j]=Î“â€‹(j+1)2â€‹Ï€â€‹âˆ«âˆ’âˆ+âˆeâˆ’(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)â€‹yâˆ—â€‹ğ”¼â€‹[Zqâ€‹e(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)â€‹Y](Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)j+1â€‹ğ‘‘u1,\displaystyle\mathbb{E}[Z^{q}(Y-y\_{\*})\_{+}^{j}]=\frac{\Gamma(j+1)}{2\pi}\int\_{-\infty}^{+\infty}e^{-(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})y\_{\*}}\frac{\mathbb{E}[Z^{q}e^{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})Y}]}{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})^{j+1}}du\_{1}, |  |

with Î±1>0\alpha\_{1}>0. Rewrite ğ”¼â€‹[Zqâ€‹e(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)â€‹Y]=dqâ€‹ğ”¼â€‹[e(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)â€‹Y+Î½â€‹Z]dâ€‹Î½q|Î½=0=Î¦(Y,Z)(0,q)â€‹(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1,0)\mathbb{E}[Z^{q}e^{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})Y}]=\frac{d^{q}\mathbb{E}\left[e^{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})Y+\nu Z}\right]}{d\nu^{q}}|\_{\nu=0}=\Phi\_{(Y,Z)}^{(0,q)}(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1},0) and substituting this expression in the equation above we reach the result after taking the real part of the integral since the left hand side is real. Applying Fubiniâ€™s theorem requires the integrability of u1âˆˆâ„â†’ğ”¼â€‹[Zqâ€‹e(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)â€‹Y](Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)j+1u\_{1}\in\mathbb{R}\to\frac{\mathbb{E}[Z^{q}e^{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})Y}]}{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})^{j+1}}.
âˆ

Note that the above result applies to a variable defined on â„2\mathbb{R}^{2}.

The computation of the conditional higher moments ([23](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E23 "In 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) instead of a two-dimensional integration ([24](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E24 "In Proposition 3.2. â€£ 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")). This result can be further extended to more variables. The proposition below provides a method to compute the cross moments of two variables, conditional on a third (dependent) variable. It is presented without proof, as it follows the same structure as the proof of PropositionÂ [3.4](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem4 "Proposition 3.4. â€£ 3.2 One-dimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.").

###### Proposition 3.5.

Let (Y,X,Z)âˆˆâ„+3(Y,X,Z)\in\mathbb{R}\_{+}^{3} be a 3-dimensional random vector and denote for (v1,v2,v3)âˆˆâ„3(v\_{1},v\_{2},v\_{3})\in\mathbb{R}^{3} its MGF by Î¦(Y,X,Z)â€‹(v1,v2,v3)\Phi\_{(Y,X,Z)}(v\_{1},v\_{2},v\_{3}). Denote Î¦(Y,X,Z)(0,r,q)â€‹(v1,v2,v3)\Phi\_{(Y,X,Z)}^{(0,r,q)}(v\_{1},v\_{2},v\_{3}) for (v1,v2,v3)âˆˆâ„3(v\_{1},v\_{2},v\_{3})\in\mathbb{R}^{3} the râ€‹-thr\text{-th} order derivative with respect to v2v\_{2} and the qq order derivative with respect to v3v\_{3} of Î¦(Y,X,Z)â€‹(v1,v2,v3)\Phi\_{(Y,X,Z)}(v\_{1},v\_{2},v\_{3}) (and 0 order derivative with respect to v1v\_{1}). Let yâˆ—âˆˆâ„+y\_{\*}\in\mathbb{R}\_{+}, Î±1âˆˆâ„+\alpha\_{1}\in\mathbb{R}\_{+} and assume suitable integrability conditions of the functions u1âˆˆâ„â†’Î¦(Y,X,Z)(0,r,q)â€‹(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1,0,0)(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)j+1u\_{1}\in\mathbb{R}\to\frac{\Phi\_{(Y,X,Z)}^{(0,r,q)}(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1},0,0)}{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})^{j+1}} for j=0,â€¦,pj=0,\ldots,p. Then we have

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ğ”¼â€‹[Ypâ€‹Xrâ€‹Zqâ€‹ğŸ{Y>yâˆ—}]=âˆ«0+âˆâˆ‘j=0p(pj)â€‹yâˆ—pâˆ’jâ€‹Î“â€‹(j+1)Ï€â€‹â„œâ¡(eâˆ’(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)â€‹yâˆ—â€‹Î¦(Y,X,Z)(0,r,q)â€‹(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1,0,0)(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)j+1)â€‹dâ€‹u1.\displaystyle\mathbb{E}[Y^{p}X^{r}Z^{q}\mathbf{1}\_{\{Y>y\_{\*}\}}]=\int\_{0}^{+\infty}\sum\_{j=0}^{p}\binom{p}{j}\frac{y\_{\*}^{p-j}\Gamma(j+1)}{\pi}\Re\left(\frac{e^{-(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})y\_{\*}}\Phi\_{(Y,X,Z)}^{(0,r,q)}(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1},0,0)}{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})^{j+1}}\right)du\_{1}. |  | (26) |

Note that the above result applies to a variable defined on â„3\mathbb{R}^{3}.

Note that ([26](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E26 "In Proposition 3.5. â€£ 3.2 One-dimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) enables the computation of ğ”¼â€‹[Xrâ€‹Zqâ€‹|Y>â€‹yâˆ—]\mathbb{E}[X^{r}Z^{q}|Y>y\_{\*}] from which we can obtain the tail joint central (higher) moment used in Yang et al. The purpose of the following remark is mainly to introduce notations that will be needed later in the work.

###### Remark 3.6.

|  | ğ”¼â€‹[âˆi=1nYipiâ€‹ğŸ{Y1>yâˆ—}]=âˆ«0+âˆâˆ‘j=0p1(p1j)â€‹yâˆ—p1âˆ’jâ€‹cjÏ€â€‹â„œâ¡(eâˆ’(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)â€‹yâˆ—â€‹Î¦(Y1,â€¦,Yn)(0,p2,â€¦,pn)â€‹(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1,0,â€¦,0)(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)j+1)â€‹dâ€‹u1,\displaystyle\mathbb{E}\left[\prod\_{i=1}^{n}Y\_{i}^{p\_{i}}\mathbf{1}\_{\{Y\_{1}>y\_{\*}\}}\right]=\int\_{0}^{+\infty}\sum\_{j=0}^{p\_{1}}\binom{p\_{1}}{j}\frac{y\_{\*}^{p\_{1}-j}c\_{j}}{\pi}\Re\left(\frac{e^{-(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})y\_{\*}}\Phi\_{(Y\_{1},...,Y\_{n})}^{(0,p\_{2},...,p\_{n})}(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1},0,...,0)}{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})^{j+1}}\right)du\_{1}, |  | (27) |

with cj=Î“â€‹(j+1)c\_{j}=\Gamma(j+1).  Note also that result can be extended without any change to a variable defined on â„n\mathbb{R}^{n}.

From ([19](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E19 "In 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")), it should be noted that any form of higher order moment or central moment can be constructed. These higher order moments are beneficial for analyzing tail risk properties. For example, the well known tail variance is defined as

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ğ”¼â€‹[(Yâˆ’ğ”¼â€‹[Yâ€‹|Y>â€‹yâˆ—])2â€‹|Y>â€‹yâˆ—]=ğ”¼â€‹[Y2â€‹|Y>â€‹yâˆ—]âˆ’ğ”¼â€‹[Yâ€‹|Y>â€‹yâˆ—]2,\mathbb{E}[(Y-\mathbb{E}[Y|Y>y\_{\*}])^{2}|Y>y\_{\*}]=\mathbb{E}[Y^{2}|Y>y\_{\*}]-\mathbb{E}[Y|Y>y\_{\*}]^{2}, |  |

and both terms can be calculated using PropositionÂ [3.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem1 "Proposition 3.1. â€£ 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."). Note that this statement applies whether YY is a sum of losses or not.

The previous propositions apply to any random vector with a known MGF  and are particularly relevant when one of the variables is a sum of random variables, as is the case with the sum of losses in a portfolio. Note that only under very specific distributions for the losses will the sum have a tractable density. This makes any methodology based on the density difficult, if not impossible, to implement. In the next section, we show how the previous expressions can be specified when working with the Wishart process. Interestingly, its process property (i.e., its time dependence) and its positive definite matrix property offer new perspectives that can be effectively addressed using the Fourier transform representation of risk measures.

### 3.3 Wishart conditional tail risk measures

In the previous section, the results were presented in a very general form. Essentially, they require the MGF, the derivative of the MGF of the state variable, as well as some integrability conditions for these functions. The purpose of this section is to show that the Wishart process satisfies these requirements.

Let (x11,t,â€¦,xnâ€‹n,t)(x\_{11,t},\ldots,x\_{nn,t}) be an nÃ—1n\times 1 vector of losses, and assume that this vector is the diagonal of a Wishart process xtx\_{t} of size nn. Note that xiâ€‹i,t=trâ€‹[Î¸1â€‹xt]x\_{ii,t}=\textup{tr}[\theta\_{1}x\_{t}] with Î¸1=eiâ€‹i\theta\_{1}=e\_{ii}. A standard risk measure associated with xiâ€‹i,tx\_{ii,t} is the qâ€‹-thq\text{-th} moment of xiâ€‹i,tx\_{ii,t} conditional on xiâ€‹i,t>xâˆ—x\_{ii,t}>x\_{\*} for a given xâˆ—âˆˆâ„+x\_{\*}\in\mathbb{R}\_{+}. It is given by the following proposition.

###### Proposition 3.7.

Assume that Ï‰=Î²â€‹Ïƒ2\omega=\beta\sigma^{2} and let Î¸1=eiâ€‹i\theta\_{1}=e\_{ii} for iâˆˆ{1,â€¦,n}i\in\{1,\ldots,n\} so that xiâ€‹i,t=trâ€‹[Î¸1â€‹xt]x\_{ii,t}=\textup{tr}[\theta\_{1}x\_{t}], then the qâ€‹-thq\text{-th} moment of trâ€‹[Î¸1â€‹xt]\textup{tr}[\theta\_{1}x\_{t}] conditional on trâ€‹[Î¸1â€‹xt]>xâˆ—\textup{tr}[\theta\_{1}x\_{t}]>x\_{\*}, with xâˆ—âˆˆâ„+x\_{\*}\in\mathbb{R}\_{+}, is given by

with sâˆ—>0s\_{\*}>0, it is the qâ€‹-thq\text{-th} moment of the losses on a portfolio conditional on the sum of these being above a certain threshold. For q=1q=1, it is TCEstâ¡(sâˆ—)\operatorname{TCE}\_{s\_{t}}(s\_{\*}), the TCE of the portfolio.

When considering several losses, the quantity of interest is the expected loss of the variable xiâ€‹i,tx\_{ii,t} conditional on the sum of losses being above a certain threshold, it is given by ğ”¼â€‹[xiâ€‹i,tâ€‹|st>â€‹sâˆ—]\mathbb{E}[x\_{ii,t}|s\_{t}>s\_{\*}]. An extension of this measure is the higher moments of xiâ€‹i,tx\_{ii,t} conditional on the sum of losses being above a certain threshold, i.e., ğ”¼â€‹[xiâ€‹i,tqâ€‹|st>â€‹sâˆ—]\mathbb{E}[x\_{ii,t}^{q}|s\_{t}>s\_{\*}]. But we can further extend from higher moments of xiâ€‹i,tx\_{ii,t} to higher cross-moments of (xiâ€‹i,t,st)(x\_{ii,t},s\_{t}) conditional on the sum of losses being above a certain threshold, i.e., ğ”¼â€‹[xiâ€‹i,tqâ€‹stpâ€‹|st>â€‹sâˆ—]\mathbb{E}[x\_{ii,t}^{q}s\_{t}^{p}|s\_{t}>s\_{\*}]. Thanks to the previous analytical results, these quantities are easy to obtain in our framework. In particular, the following proposition derives from Proposition [3.2](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem2 "Proposition 3.2. â€£ 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.").

As previously mentioned, the above result is of interest but it involves a multi-dimensional integration. However, PropositionÂ [3.4](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem4 "Proposition 3.4. â€£ 3.2 One-dimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. As CorollariesÂ [2.4](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S2.Thmtheorem4 "Corollary 2.4. â€£ 2 The mathematical framework â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. The usual caveat applies.") clearly demonstrate, the Wishart process possesses this property. The proof of the following proposition is a straightforward consequence of PropositionÂ [3.4](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem4 "Proposition 3.4. â€£ 3.2 One-dimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. ###### Proposition 3.9.

Let Î¸0=âˆ‘i=1neiâ€‹i\theta\_{0}=\sum\_{i=1}^{n}e\_{ii} and Î¸1=eiâ€‹i\theta\_{1}=e\_{ii} for iâˆˆ{1,â€¦,n}i\in\{1,\ldots,n\} so that st=trâ€‹[Î¸0â€‹xt]s\_{t}=\textup{tr}[\theta\_{0}x\_{t}] and xiâ€‹i,t=trâ€‹[Î¸1â€‹xt]x\_{ii,t}=\textup{tr}[\theta\_{1}x\_{t}]. Then the (pâ€‹-th,qâ€‹-th)(p\text{-th},q\text{-th}) moment of (trâ€‹[Î¸0â€‹xt],trâ€‹[Î¸1â€‹xt])(\textup{tr}[\theta\_{0}x\_{t}],\textup{tr}[\theta\_{1}x\_{t}]) conditional on the event st>sâˆ—s\_{t}>s\_{\*}, with sâˆ—âˆˆâ„+s\_{\*}\in\mathbb{R}\_{+}, can be written as

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ğ”¼â€‹[trâ€‹[Î¸0â€‹xt]pâ€‹trâ€‹[Î¸1â€‹xt]qâ€‹|trâ€‹[Î¸0â€‹xt]>â€‹sâˆ—]=âˆ«0+âˆâˆ‘j=0p(pj)â€‹sâˆ—pâˆ’jâ€‹cjâ€‹â„œâ¡(eâˆ’(Î±0âˆ’iâ€‹u0)â€‹sâˆ—â€‹Î¦(trâ€‹[Î¸0â€‹xt],trâ€‹[Î¸1â€‹xt])(0,q)â€‹(Î±0âˆ’iâ€‹u0,0)(Î±0âˆ’iâ€‹u0)j+1)â€‹dâ€‹u0âˆ«0+âˆâ„œâ¡(eâˆ’(Î±0âˆ’iâ€‹u0)â€‹sâˆ—â€‹Î¦trâ€‹[Î¸0â€‹xt]â€‹(Î±0âˆ’iâ€‹u0)(Î±0âˆ’iâ€‹u0))â€‹ğ‘‘u0,\displaystyle\mathbb{E}\left[\textup{tr}[\theta\_{0}x\_{t}]^{p}\textup{tr}[\theta\_{1}x\_{t}]^{q}|\textup{tr}[\theta\_{0}x\_{t}]>s\_{\*}\right]=\frac{\int\_{0}^{+\infty}\sum\_{j=0}^{p}\binom{p}{j}s\_{\*}^{p-j}c\_{j}\Re\left(\frac{e^{-(\alpha\_{0}-\mathrm{i}u\_{0})s\_{\*}}\Phi\_{(\textup{tr}[\theta\_{0}x\_{t}],\textup{tr}[\theta\_{1}x\_{t}])}^{(0,q)}(\alpha\_{0}-\mathrm{i}u\_{0},0)}{(\alpha\_{0}-\mathrm{i}u\_{0})^{j+1}}\right)du\_{0}}{\int\_{0}^{+\infty}\Re\left(\frac{e^{-(\alpha\_{0}-\mathrm{i}u\_{0})s\_{\*}}\Phi\_{\textup{tr}[\theta\_{0}x\_{t}]}(\alpha\_{0}-\mathrm{i}u\_{0})}{(\alpha\_{0}-\mathrm{i}u\_{0})}\right)du\_{0}}, |  | (31) |

Note that no order is specified on Î¸1\theta\_{1} and Î¸2\theta\_{2}, and so we can interchange these matrices at will. This means we can easily compute the cross-moments by conditioning on the individual losses xiâ€‹i,tx\_{ii,t} or on the portfolio itself âˆ‘i=1nxiâ€‹i,t\sum\_{i=1}^{n}x\_{ii,t}.

Still in a portfolio perspective, in our framework we not only specify the distribution of losses but also their dependencies, which can be used to perform conditioning. Let Î¸0=(e12+e21)/2\theta\_{0}=(e\_{12}+e\_{21})/2, then x12,t=trâ€‹[Î¸0â€‹xt]x\_{12,t}=\textup{tr}[\theta\_{0}x\_{t}]. Similarly, let Î¸1=e11\theta\_{1}=e\_{11} and Î¸2=e22\theta\_{2}=e\_{22}, so that x11,t=trâ€‹[Î¸1â€‹xt]x\_{11,t}=\textup{tr}[\theta\_{1}x\_{t}] and x22,t=trâ€‹[Î¸2â€‹xt]x\_{22,t}=\textup{tr}[\theta\_{2}x\_{t}]. We can then calculate

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ğ”¼â€‹[x11,tpâ€‹x22,tqâ€‹|x12,t>â€‹xâˆ—],\displaystyle\mathbb{E}[x\_{11,t}^{p}x\_{22,t}^{q}|x\_{12,t}>x\_{\*}], |  | (32) |

which is the expected cross-moment of the first loss and the second loss conditional on the covariance between these losses being above a certain threshold. This example exploits the positive definite matrix nature of the Wishart process. The proposition below is an application of PropositionÂ [3.5](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem5 "Proposition 3.5. â€£ 3.2 One-dimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."), which allows us to compute such a conditional cross-moment of the Wishart process.

###### Proposition 3.10.

Consider Î¸0=(e12+e21)/2\theta\_{0}=(e\_{12}+e\_{21})/2, Î¸1=e11\theta\_{1}=e\_{11}, and Î¸2=e22\theta\_{2}=e\_{22} so that x12,t=trâ€‹[Î¸0â€‹xt]x\_{12,t}=\textup{tr}[\theta\_{0}x\_{t}], x11,t=trâ€‹[Î¸1â€‹xt]x\_{11,t}=\textup{tr}[\theta\_{1}x\_{t}] and x22,t=trâ€‹[Î¸2â€‹xt]x\_{22,t}=\textup{tr}[\theta\_{2}x\_{t}]. For a given pair (p,q)âˆˆâ„•2(p,q)\in\mathbb{N}^{2} and xâˆ—âˆˆâ„+x\_{\*}\in\mathbb{R}\_{+}, we have

|  |  |  |  |

|  | ğ”¼â€‹[trâ€‹[Î¸1â€‹xt]pâ€‹trâ€‹[Î¸2â€‹xt]qâ€‹|trâ€‹[Î¸0â€‹xt]>â€‹xâˆ—]=âˆ«0+âˆâ„œâ¡(eâˆ’(Î±0âˆ’iâ€‹u0)â€‹xâˆ—â€‹Î¦(trâ€‹[Î¸0â€‹xt],trâ€‹[Î¸1â€‹xt],trâ€‹[Î¸2â€‹xt])(0,p,q)â€‹(Î±0âˆ’iâ€‹u0,0,0)(Î±0âˆ’iâ€‹u0))â€‹ğ‘‘u0âˆ«0+âˆâ„œâ¡(eâˆ’(Î±0âˆ’iâ€‹u0)â€‹xâˆ—â€‹Î¦trâ€‹[Î¸0â€‹xt]â€‹(Î±0âˆ’iâ€‹u0)(Î±0âˆ’iâ€‹u0))â€‹ğ‘‘u0,\displaystyle\mathbb{E}\left[\textup{tr}[\theta\_{1}x\_{t}]^{p}\textup{tr}[\theta\_{2}x\_{t}]^{q}|\textup{tr}[\theta\_{0}x\_{t}]>x\_{\*}\right]=\frac{\int\_{0}^{+\infty}\Re\left(\frac{e^{-(\alpha\_{0}-\mathrm{i}u\_{0})x\_{\*}}\Phi\_{(\textup{tr}[\theta\_{0}x\_{t}],\textup{tr}[\theta\_{1}x\_{t}],\textup{tr}[\theta\_{2}x\_{t}])}^{(0,p,q)}(\alpha\_{0}-\mathrm{i}u\_{0},0,0)}{(\alpha\_{0}-\mathrm{i}u\_{0})}\right)du\_{0}}{\int\_{0}^{+\infty}\Re\left(\frac{e^{-(\alpha\_{0}-\mathrm{i}u\_{0})x\_{\*}}\Phi\_{\textup{tr}[\theta\_{0}x\_{t}]}(\alpha\_{0}-\mathrm{i}u\_{0})}{(\alpha\_{0}-\mathrm{i}u\_{0})}\right)du\_{0}}, |  | (33) |

The usual caveat applies.") and CorollaryÂ [2.4](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S2.Thmtheorem4 "Corollary 2.4. â€£ 2 The mathematical framework â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.").

Note that x12,tx\_{12,t} can be either positive or negative. As per the remark that follows Proposition [3.2](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem2 "Proposition 3.2. â€£ 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. The usual caveat applies."), one has to use either Bateman and ErdÃ©lyi ([1954](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib46 "Tables of integral transforms"), 3.2(3)), leading to Î±0>0\alpha\_{0}>0, or Bateman and ErdÃ©lyi ([1954](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib46 "Tables of integral transforms"), 3.2(4)) leading to Î±0<0\alpha\_{0}<0.

###### Remark 3.11.

As Equation ([29](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E29 "In 3.3 Wishart conditional tail risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) shows, Proposition [3.7](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem7 "Proposition 3.7. â€£ 3.3 Wishart conditional tail risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.") applies to a portfolio, while Propositions [3.9](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem9 "Proposition 3.9. â€£ 3.3 Wishart conditional tail risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.") and [3.10](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem10 "Proposition 3.10. â€£ 3.3 Wishart conditional tail risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.") demonstrate how to compute higher (conditional) cross-moments. The Wishart distribution is an example of a distribution for which computing these risk measures using the density leads to significant numerical difficulties, and in particular when the conditioning variable in the sum of dependent losses. Note also that the framework, both the methodology and the chosen distribution on the space of symmetric positive definite matrices, allows for the determination of these risk measures even when one (or several) of the variables controlling the dependency of the distribution is involved. This dependency can be fairly general; in particular, it can take any sign, which contrasts with existing results (see Furman and Landsman ([2005](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib41 "Risk capital decomposition for a multivariate dependent gamma portfolio"), Definition 1, Condition 5) or Blier-Wong et al. ([2025](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib10 "Efficient evaluation of risk allocations"), Examples 6.1 and 6.2)), where there is a sign constraint because the state variable is a vector of independent random variables, and the dependence derives from one of the variable being a common factor to the losses.

Let us mention the two recent interesting works Arias-Serna et al. ([2021](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib14 "Risk measures: A generalization from the univariate to the matrix-variate")) and Arias-Serna et al. ([2025](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib13 "Matrix-variate risk measures under Wishart and gamma distributions")), which compute the VaR, not a coherent risk measure, using the density of the state variable following a Wishart distribution. Compared to these works, the above formula give conditional higher moments, and by formulating the problem in terms of the MGF, the methodology remains numerically simple to implement since the density of the Wishart process, besides depending of many variables, involves a special function of matrix argument that is challenging to evaluate. In contrast, the MGF of the Wishart distribution only involves the ratio of matrices and the determinant of matrices, both functions are simple to derive. This aspect is crucial to obtain the above formulas.

The above propositions, while daunting at first glance, are easily computable in most programming languages.

#### 3.3.1 The two dates case

We can take advantage of the time-dependent nature of the Wishart process by considering losses at two different dates. In this particular case, one is interested in the intertemporal or time-lagged properties of the risk measures, which are most often analyzed using static distributions.  This perspective relates to the time-series literature on risk measures, see for example, Chavez-Demoulin and Guillou ([2018](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib3 "Extreme quantile estimation for Î²-mixing time series and applications")) or Goegebeur and Guillou ([2024](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib5 "A conditional tail expectation type risk measure for time series")). Interestingly, it can also be related the literature on (multivariate) count processes (such as the Cox process), where one models two (or more) events (in our case, losses), and their dependence (see Lu et al. ([2024](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib18 "Cyber risk modeling: a discrete multivariate count process approach"))). The temporal nature of this problem often involves leveraging the autocorrelation of a single loss or the correlation between two types of losses occurring at different times. Within the context of the present work, this translates as follows.

Given two dates t0,t1âˆˆâ„+t\_{0},t\_{1}\in\mathbb{R}\_{+} such that 0<t0<t10<t\_{0}<t\_{1}, we are interested in the quantities ğ”¼â€‹[xiâ€‹i,t1qâ€‹|xiâ€‹i,t0>â€‹xâˆ—]\mathbb{E}\left[x\_{ii,t\_{1}}^{q}|x\_{ii,t\_{0}}>x\_{\*}\right], ğ”¼â€‹[st1pâ€‹|st0>â€‹sâˆ—]\mathbb{E}\left[s\_{t\_{1}}^{p}|s\_{t\_{0}}>s\_{\*}\right], ğ”¼â€‹[st1pâ€‹xiâ€‹i,t1qâ€‹|st0>â€‹sâˆ—]\mathbb{E}\left[s\_{t\_{1}}^{p}x\_{ii,t\_{1}}^{q}|s\_{t\_{0}}>s\_{\*}\right] with xâˆ—>0x\_{\*}>0, sâˆ—>0s\_{\*}>0 and p,qâˆˆâ„•p,q\in\mathbb{N}. For example, the first (conditional) expectation represents the expected value of the qâ€‹-thq\text{-th} moment of the ithi^{\text{th}} loss at time t1t\_{1} conditional on the event that at the previous time t0t\_{0} this loss was greater than xâˆ—x\_{\*}. The other expectations can be interpreted in a similar way. Thanks to PropositionÂ [2.5](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S2.Thmtheorem5 "Proposition 2.5. â€£ 2 The mathematical framework â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."), PropositionÂ [2.6](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S2.Thmtheorem6 "Proposition 2.6. â€£ 2 The mathematical framework â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."), CorollaryÂ [2.7](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S2.Thmtheorem7 "Corollary 2.7. â€£ 2 The mathematical framework â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. The usual caveat applies.") and Proposition [3.4](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem4 "Proposition 3.4. â€£ 3.2 One-dimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. Let us formulate the result in very general terms, with all these conditional expectations being special cases.
