### 3.4 A note on numerical precision

In this section, we contextualize our results within the broader literature. We first show how our formulae align with common notational conventions, and then demonstrate how they can be applied to well-known distributions whose MGFs are already established in the literature.

A commonly encountered quantity is the TCE of a random variable YY at a threshold yâˆ—y\_{\*} that is defined as:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | TCEYâ¡(yâˆ—)=ğ”¼â€‹[Yâ€‹âˆ£Y>â€‹yâˆ—].\operatorname{TCE}\_{Y}(y\_{\*})=\mathbb{E}[Y\mid Y>y\_{\*}]. |  |

Using ([19](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E19 "In 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) and PropositionÂ [3.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem1 "Proposition 3.1. â€£ 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."), we can compute TCEYâ¡(yâˆ—)\operatorname{TCE}\_{Y}(y\_{\*}) exactly from the MGF Î¦Yâ€‹(â‹…)\Phi\_{Y}(\cdot). This approach involves no approximation other than standard numerical integration. Notably, this method also extends to the sum of dependent random variables, S=âˆ‘i=1nYiS=\sum\_{i=1}^{n}Y\_{i}, provided the MGF Î¦(Y1,â€¦,Yn)â€‹(â‹…,â€¦,â‹…)\Phi\_{(Y\_{1},...,Y\_{n})}(\cdot,...,\cdot) is known since Î¦Sâ€‹(z)=Î¦(Y1,â€¦,Yn)â€‹(z,â€¦,z)\Phi\_{S}(z)=\Phi\_{(Y\_{1},...,Y\_{n})}(z,...,z) for zâˆˆâ„z\in\mathbb{R} is known. Thus, the approach remains entirely general.

One might argue that numerical integration is an approximation. However, it is important to emphasize that most â€˜closed-formâ€™ results in the literature already involve integrals that must be evaluated numerically. For example, consider the generalized hyperbolic (GH) distribution of Ignatieva and Landsman ([2019](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib42 "Conditional tail risk measures for the skewed generalised hyperbolic family")), where a random vector is defined to be a GH distribution, (Y1,â€¦,Yn)âˆ¼Gâ€‹Hnâ€‹(Î»,Ï‡,Ïˆ,ğ,Î£,ğœ¸)(Y\_{1},...,Y\_{n})\sim GH\_{n}(\lambda,\chi,\psi,\boldsymbol{\mu},\Sigma,\boldsymbol{\gamma}), if its MGF is given for ğ¯âˆˆâ„n\mathbf{v}\in\mathbb{R}^{n} by

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Î¦(Y1,â€¦,Yn)â€‹(ğ¯)=expâ¡(ğ¯âŠ¤â€‹ğ)â€‹(ÏˆÏˆâˆ’2â€‹ğ¯âŠ¤â€‹ğœ¸âˆ’ğ¯âŠ¤â€‹Î£â€‹ğ¯)Î»/2â€‹KÎ»â€‹(Ï‡â€‹(Ïˆâˆ’2â€‹ğ¯âŠ¤â€‹ğœ¸âˆ’ğ¯âŠ¤â€‹Î£â€‹ğ¯))KÎ»â€‹(Ï‡â€‹Ïˆ),\displaystyle\Phi\_{(Y\_{1},...,Y\_{n})}(\mathbf{v})=\exp(\mathbf{v}^{\top}\boldsymbol{\mu})\left(\frac{\psi}{\psi-2\mathbf{v}^{\top}\boldsymbol{\gamma}-\mathbf{v}^{\top}\Sigma\mathbf{v}}\right)^{\lambda/2}\frac{K\_{\lambda}\left(\sqrt{\chi\left(\psi-2\mathbf{v}^{\top}\boldsymbol{\gamma}-\mathbf{v}^{\top}\Sigma\mathbf{v}\right)}\right)}{K\_{\lambda}\left(\sqrt{\chi\psi}\right)}, |  | (35) |

where KÎ»â€‹(â‹…)K\_{\lambda}(\cdot) is the modified Bessel function of the third kind, see Ignatieva and Landsman ([2019](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib42 "Conditional tail risk measures for the skewed generalised hyperbolic family"), Eq.Â (2.6)). Our integral-based approach can directly use this MGF and the known derivatives of KÎ»â€‹(â‹…)K\_{\lambda}(\cdot) (see DLMF ([2010](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib45 "Digital library of mathematical functions"), Eq.Â (10.29.2))) to produce all desired tail measures without further approximation. Alternatively, the key result from Ignatieva and Landsman ([2019](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib42 "Conditional tail risk measures for the skewed generalised hyperbolic family")) computes the TCE of a (univariate) GH distribution through their Theorem 3.1, which is

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | ÏˆÎ»â€‹(Ïˆ+Î³2â€‹Ïƒâˆ’2)12âˆ’Î»â€‹(Ï‡â€‹Ïˆ)âˆ’Î»2â€‹Ï€â€‹Ïƒâ€‹KÎ»â€‹(Ï‡â€‹Ïˆ)â€‹KÎ»âˆ’12â€‹((Ï‡+Q)â€‹(Ïˆ+Î³2â€‹Ïƒâˆ’2))((Ï‡+Q)â€‹(Ïˆ+Î³2â€‹Ïƒâˆ’2))12âˆ’Î»â€‹e(yâˆ’Î¼)â€‹Î³â€‹Ïƒâˆ’2,\displaystyle\frac{\psi^{\lambda}(\psi+\gamma^{2}\sigma^{-2})^{\frac{1}{2}-\lambda}\left(\sqrt{\chi\psi}\right)^{-\lambda}}{\sqrt{2\pi}\sigma K\_{\lambda}(\sqrt{\chi\psi})}\frac{K\_{\lambda-\frac{1}{2}}\left(\sqrt{(\chi+Q)(\psi+\gamma^{2}\sigma^{-2})}\right)}{\left(\sqrt{(\chi+Q)(\psi+\gamma^{2}\sigma^{-2})}\right)^{\frac{1}{2}-\lambda}}e^{(y-\mu)\gamma\sigma^{-2}}, |  | (38) |

where detâ€‹(Î£)12=Ïƒ\textup{det}(\Sigma)^{\frac{1}{2}}=\sigma, and Q=(yâˆ’Î¼)2â€‹Ïƒâˆ’2Q=(y-\mu)^{2}\sigma^{-2}, see Ignatieva and Landsman ([2019](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib42 "Conditional tail risk measures for the skewed generalised hyperbolic family"), Eq. (2.7)). The survival function FÂ¯GH1â€‹(yq;Î»+1,Ï‡,Ïˆ,Î¼,Ïƒ2,Î³)\bar{F}\_{\mathrm{GH}\_{1}}(y\_{q};\lambda+1,\chi,\psi,\mu,\sigma^{2},\gamma) of the GH distribution is given by 1 minus the integral of the density function fGâ€‹H1â€‹(yq;Î»+1,Ï‡,Ïˆ,Î¼,Ïƒ2,Î³)f\_{GH\_{1}}(y\_{q};\lambda+1,\chi,\psi,\mu,\sigma^{2},\gamma) and kÎ»k\_{\lambda} is a constant satisfying

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | kÎ»=Ï‡Ïˆâ€‹KÎ»+1â€‹(Ï‡â€‹Ïˆ)KÎ»â€‹(Ï‡â€‹Ïˆ).\displaystyle k\_{\lambda}=\sqrt{\frac{\chi}{\psi}}\frac{K\_{\lambda+1}(\sqrt{\chi\psi})}{K\_{\lambda}(\sqrt{\chi\psi})}. |  | (39) |

As we can see, Theorem 3.1 of Ignatieva and Landsman ([2019](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib42 "Conditional tail risk measures for the skewed generalised hyperbolic family")) requires an integration due to the survival function FÂ¯Gâ€‹H1â€‹(y)\bar{F}\_{GH\_{1}}(y), where our results also only require a one-dimensional integration. However, our approach also has the flexibility to calculate conditional higher moments as we shall see below.

When considering a sum of losses, the TCE of the sum can be computed thanks to a formula of the form ([36](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E36 "In 3.4 A note on numerical precision â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) since if (Y1,â€¦,Yn)âˆ¼Gâ€‹Hnâ€‹(Î»,Ï‡,Ïˆ,ğ,Î£,ğœ¸)(Y\_{1},...,Y\_{n})\sim GH\_{n}(\lambda,\chi,\psi,\boldsymbol{\mu},\Sigma,\boldsymbol{\gamma}) then S=âˆ‘i=1nYiS=\sum\_{i=1}^{n}Y\_{i} follows the distribution Gâ€‹H1â€‹(Î»,Ï‡,Ïˆ,1âŠ¤â€‹ğ,1âŠ¤â€‹Î£â€‹1,1âŠ¤â€‹ğœ¸)GH\_{1}(\lambda,\chi,\psi,\textbf{1}^{\top}\boldsymbol{\mu},\textbf{1}^{\top}\Sigma\textbf{1},\textbf{1}^{\top}\boldsymbol{\gamma}) with 1=(1,â€¦,1)âŠ¤\textbf{1}=(1,\ldots,1)^{\top} an nn-dimensional vector of ones. It is this property of the GH distribution that ensures a simple expression for the density of the sum that keeps the computation of the TCE a one-dimensional integration problem even in the multivariate case. Note that for many distributions, and in particular for the Wishart distribution, the density of the sum does not admit a simple expression, making the computation of the TCE of the sum challenging.

Furthermore, Ignatieva and Landsman ([2019](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib42 "Conditional tail risk measures for the skewed generalised hyperbolic family"), Theorem 3.2) show that the TCE of the sum can be decomposed as a sum of expectations of losses conditional on the sum being above a certain threshold. These conditional expectations are of the form ğ”¼â€‹[Yiâ€‹|S>â€‹sâˆ—]\mathbb{E}[Y\_{i}|S>s\_{\*}] and thanks to the property of the GH distribution they can admit an expression of the form ([36](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E36 "In 3.4 A note on numerical precision â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) (with adjusted parameters). From a numerical point of view, it amounts to perform several one-dimensional integrations. With our approach, since the MGF of (Y1,â€¦,Yn)(Y\_{1},...,Y\_{n}) is known, the results can also be obtained at the same numerical cost.777A worked-out implementation of the TCE\operatorname{TCE} for the GH distribution, computed using the density as in Ignatieva and Landsman ([2019](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib42 "Conditional tail risk measures for the skewed generalised hyperbolic family")) and our approach, is provided in the supplementary appendix.

Thus, the numerical cost, the precision and accuracy of our results are comparable to, and in many cases equivalent to, methods currently in use. However, our approach applies to distributions for which the density of the sum is not simple to compute, and the Wishart distribution is one of them.

As previously noted, our approach not only applies to a wide range of distributions but also enables the computation of conditional higher moments, as demonstrated in the following section.

### 3.5 Conditional higher moments tail risk measures

Beyond the TCE, our methodology readily extends to other tail-based risk measures, and when considering the risk measures of a sum of losses, it naturally introduces conditional higher moments of losses.

##### The Tail variance (TV):

The tail variance, defined as the conditional second central moment given Y>yâˆ—Y>y\_{\*}, can be written as:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | TVYâ¡(yâˆ—)=ğ”¼â€‹[(Yâˆ’ğ”¼â€‹[Yâ€‹|Y>â€‹yâˆ—])2â€‹âˆ£Y>â€‹yâˆ—]=ğ”¼â€‹[Y2â€‹âˆ£Y>â€‹yâˆ—]âˆ’(ğ”¼â€‹[Yâ€‹âˆ£Y>â€‹yâˆ—])2.\displaystyle\operatorname{TV}\_{Y}(y\_{\*})=\mathbb{E}[(Y-\mathbb{E}[Y|Y>y\_{\*}])^{2}\mid Y>y\_{\*}]=\mathbb{E}[Y^{2}\mid Y>y\_{\*}]-(\mathbb{E}[Y\mid Y>y\_{\*}])^{2}. |  | (40) |

Both ğ”¼â€‹[Y2â€‹âˆ£Y>â€‹yâˆ—]\mathbb{E}[Y^{2}\mid Y>y\_{\*}] and ğ”¼â€‹[Yâ€‹âˆ£Y>â€‹yâˆ—]\mathbb{E}[Y\mid Y>y\_{\*}] are computable using our framework as aforementioned. Whether YY is an individual loss or a sum of losses has no impact on the computational cost. However, when YY is a sum of losses, it naturally introduces the tail covariance.

##### The Tail covariance (TCov):

Consider the sum S=Y1+Y2S=Y\_{1}+Y\_{2} of two losses, we illustrate the problem using two losses but the results can be extended to higher dimension, and assume that the MGF Î¦(Y1,Y2)\Phi\_{(Y\_{1},Y\_{2})} is known. As mentioned above, we can compute TCESâ¡(sâˆ—)\operatorname{TCE}\_{S}(s^{\*}), and we can also decompose it into individual contributions since we have:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | TCESâ¡(sâˆ—)=ğ”¼â€‹[Y1â€‹|S>â€‹sâˆ—]+ğ”¼â€‹[Y2â€‹|S>â€‹sâˆ—].\operatorname{TCE}\_{S}(s^{\*})=\mathbb{E}[Y\_{1}|S>s\_{\*}]+\mathbb{E}[Y\_{2}|S>s\_{\*}]. |  |

This decomposition helps in understanding the contribution of each component variable to the tail behavior of the sum. This quantity can be calculated using PropositionÂ [3.4](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem4 "Proposition 3.4. â€£ 3.2 One-dimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."). Then considering the tail variance risk of the sum, it leads to a decomposition of the form:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | TVSâ¡(sâˆ—)=TVY1+Y2â¡(sâˆ—)=TVY1|Sâ¡(sâˆ—)+TVY2|Sâ¡(sâˆ—)+2â€‹TCovY1,Y2|Sâ¡(sâˆ—),\displaystyle\operatorname{TV}\_{S}(s\_{\*})=\operatorname{TV}\_{Y\_{1}+Y\_{2}}(s\_{\*})=\operatorname{TV}\_{Y\_{1}|S}(s\_{\*})+\operatorname{TV}\_{Y\_{2}|S}(s\_{\*})+2\operatorname{TCov}\_{Y\_{1},Y\_{2}|S}(s\_{\*}), |  | (41) |

where TVY1|Sâ¡(sâˆ—)=ğ”¼â€‹[(Y1âˆ’ğ”¼â€‹[Y1â€‹|S>â€‹sâˆ—])2â€‹âˆ£S>â€‹sâˆ—]=ğ”¼â€‹[Y12â€‹âˆ£S>â€‹sâˆ—]âˆ’ğ”¼â€‹[Y1â€‹|S>â€‹sâˆ—]2\operatorname{TV}\_{Y\_{1}|S}(s\_{\*})=\mathbb{E}[(Y\_{1}-\mathbb{E}[Y\_{1}|S>s\_{\*}])^{2}\mid S>s\_{\*}]=\mathbb{E}[Y\_{1}^{2}\mid S>s\_{\*}]-\mathbb{E}[Y\_{1}|S>s\_{\*}]^{2}, a similar equation for TVY2|Sâ¡(sâˆ—)\operatorname{TV}\_{Y\_{2}|S}(s\_{\*}), and the tail covariance defined as

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | TCovY1,Y2|Sâ¡(sâˆ—)=ğ”¼â€‹[Y1â€‹Y2â€‹âˆ£S>â€‹sâˆ—]âˆ’ğ”¼â€‹[Y1â€‹âˆ£S>â€‹sâˆ—]â€‹ğ”¼â€‹[Y2â€‹âˆ£S>â€‹sâˆ—],\displaystyle\operatorname{TCov}\_{Y\_{1},Y\_{2}|S}(s\_{\*})=\mathbb{E}[Y\_{1}Y\_{2}\mid S>s\_{\*}]-\mathbb{E}[Y\_{1}\mid S>s\_{\*}]\mathbb{E}[Y\_{2}\mid S>s\_{\*}], |  | (42) |

which provides insight into how dependence structures behave in the tail regions. Using our PropositionÂ [3.4](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem4 "Proposition 3.4. â€£ 3.2 One-dimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.") and PropositionÂ [3.5](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem5 "Proposition 3.5. â€£ 3.2 One-dimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."), all these conditional expectations can be exactly computed using one-dimensional integrations. Note that TCovY1,S|Sâ¡(sâˆ—)\operatorname{TCov}\_{Y\_{1},S|S}(s\_{\*}) corresponds to the tail covariance risk measure of Furman and Landsman ([2006](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib21 "Tail variance premium with applications for elliptical portfolio of risks"), Eq.Â (1.12)).

This showcases how joint distributions can yield decompositions of more complex tail risk measures, in particular for moments higher than two.

##### The Tail skewness (TS):

Following the definition of the tail variance, it is natural to define the tail skewness as:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | TSYâ¡(yâˆ—)=ğ”¼â€‹[(Yâˆ’ğ”¼â€‹[Yâ€‹|Y>â€‹yâˆ—])3â€‹âˆ£Y>â€‹yâˆ—](ğ”¼â€‹[(Yâˆ’ğ”¼â€‹[Yâ€‹|Y>â€‹yâˆ—])2â€‹âˆ£Y>â€‹yâˆ—])3/2.\displaystyle\operatorname{TS}\_{Y}(y\_{\*})=\frac{\mathbb{E}[(Y-\mathbb{E}[Y|Y>y\_{\*}])^{3}\mid Y>y\_{\*}]}{\left(\mathbb{E}[(Y-\mathbb{E}[Y|Y>y\_{\*}])^{2}\mid Y>y\_{\*}]\right)^{3/2}}. |  | (43) |

It can similarly be computed once we have the higher conditional moments, all available via our integral transforms.

If we consider the tail skewness of the sum S=Y1+Y2S=Y\_{1}+Y\_{2} of two losses, then the denominator of ([43](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E43 "In The Tail skewness (TS): â€£ 3.5 Conditional higher moments tail risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) is simply TVSâ¡(sâˆ—)\operatorname{TV}\_{S}(s\_{\*}) given by ([41](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E41 "In The Tail covariance (TCov): â€£ 3.5 Conditional higher moments tail risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")), and straightforward computations show that the numerator of ([43](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E43 "In The Tail skewness (TS): â€£ 3.5 Conditional higher moments tail risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) can be decomposed as

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ğ”¼â€‹[(Sâˆ’ğ”¼â€‹[Sâ€‹|S>â€‹sâˆ—])3â€‹âˆ£S>â€‹sâˆ—]\displaystyle\mathbb{E}[(S-\mathbb{E}[S|S>s\_{\*}])^{3}\mid S>s\_{\*}] | =ğ”¼â€‹[Y13â€‹âˆ£S>â€‹sâˆ—]+3â€‹ğ”¼â€‹[Y12â€‹Y2â€‹âˆ£S>â€‹sâˆ—]+3â€‹ğ”¼â€‹[Y1â€‹Y22â€‹âˆ£S>â€‹sâˆ—]\displaystyle=\mathbb{E}[Y\_{1}^{3}\mid S>s\_{\*}]+3\mathbb{E}[Y\_{1}^{2}Y\_{2}\mid S>s\_{\*}]+3\mathbb{E}[Y\_{1}Y\_{2}^{2}\mid S>s\_{\*}] |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | +ğ”¼[Y23âˆ£S>sâˆ—]âˆ’3TVS(sâˆ—)TCES(sâˆ—)+2TCES(sâˆ—)3,\displaystyle+\mathbb{E}[Y\_{2}^{3}\mid S>s\_{\*}]-3\operatorname{TV}\_{S}(s\_{\*})\operatorname{TCE}\_{S}(s\_{\*})+2\operatorname{TCE}\_{S}(s\_{\*})^{3}, |  |

with these conditional higher joint moments of Y1,Y2Y\_{1},Y\_{2}, that is, conditional expectations of the form ğ”¼â€‹[Y1pâ€‹Y2qâ€‹|S>â€‹sâˆ—]\mathbb{E}[Y\_{1}^{p}Y\_{2}^{q}|S>s\_{\*}] with p,qâˆˆâ„•p,q\in\mathbb{N} and p+q=3p+q=3, computed thanks to our PropositionÂ [3.4](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem4 "Proposition 3.4. â€£ 3.2 One-dimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.") and PropositionÂ [3.5](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem5 "Proposition 3.5. â€£ 3.2 One-dimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."). This latter conditional expectation is named tail joint moment in Yang et al. ([2025](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib27 "Tail moments and tail joint moments for multivariate generalized hyperbolic distribution"), Eq.Â (1.4)) and is a building block for the tail joint central moment in Yang et al. ([2025](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib27 "Tail moments and tail joint moments for multivariate generalized hyperbolic distribution"), Eq.Â (1.5)). The tail skewness appears in Yang et al. ([2025](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib27 "Tail moments and tail joint moments for multivariate generalized hyperbolic distribution")) (where it is named tail conditional skewness (TCS)), this work also defines the tail conditional kurtosis that can be handled in our framework.888A worked-out implementation of the TV\operatorname{TV} for the GH distribution, computed using the density as in Ignatieva and Landsman ([2025](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib44 "Tail variance for generalised hyper-elliptical models")) and our approach, is provided in the supplementary appendix. This appendix also contains an implementation of TS\operatorname{TS} using our approach, since it has not yet been derived using the density.

## 4 Numerical experiments

In this section, we present a numerical implementation to demonstrate the effectiveness of our formulas. We begin by detailing the implementation steps that control the dependency between losses in our model. Since our approach relies on the MGF of the state variable rather than its density, we also briefly review the well-known results that allow us to recover the key quantities used in risk measurement.

### 4.1 Implementation details

In this section, we consider the two-dimensional case n=2n=2 and illustrate our results using the synthetic parameters listed in TableÂ [1](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.T1 "Table 1 â€£ Tables â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.").

[ Insert TableÂ [1](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.T1 "Table 1 â€£ Tables â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.") here ]

We set Î²\beta in accordance with the Bru case as defined by Bru ([1991](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib85 "Wishart processes")) for computational efficiency. Additionally, we set the initial value x0x\_{0} to be the mean value of the stationary solution of the stochastic differential equation ([1](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S2.E1 "In 2 The mathematical framework â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")), it is given by the matrix xÂ¯âˆ\bar{x}\_{\infty} which is the solution of âˆ’Î²â€‹Ïƒ2=mâ€‹xÂ¯âˆ+xÂ¯âˆâ€‹mâŠ¤-\beta\sigma^{2}=m\bar{x}\_{\infty}+\bar{x}\_{\infty}m^{\top}. This solution is well defined since it is a Lyapunov equation and we assume that the eigenvalues of mm have negative real parts (Î²â€‹Ïƒ2\beta\sigma^{2} is a symmetric definite positive matrix by construction).

From ([1](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S2.E1 "In 2 The mathematical framework â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")), we can deduce the instantaneous covariance structure between the components of the Wishart process as follows:

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | dâ€‹âŸ¨x11,.,x11,.âŸ©t\displaystyle d\langle x\_{11,.},x\_{11,.}\rangle\_{t} | =4â€‹x11,tâ€‹(Ïƒ112+Ïƒ122)â€‹dâ€‹t,\displaystyle=4x\_{11,t}(\sigma\_{11}^{2}+\sigma\_{12}^{2})dt, |  | (44) |
|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | dâ€‹âŸ¨x22,.,x22,.âŸ©t\displaystyle d\langle x\_{22,.},x\_{22,.}\rangle\_{t} | =4â€‹x22,tâ€‹(Ïƒ122+Ïƒ222)â€‹dâ€‹t,\displaystyle=4x\_{22,t}(\sigma\_{12}^{2}+\sigma\_{22}^{2})dt, |  | (45) |
|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | dâ€‹âŸ¨x12,.,x12,.âŸ©t\displaystyle d\langle x\_{12,.},x\_{12,.}\rangle\_{t} | =x11,tâ€‹(Ïƒ122+Ïƒ222)â€‹dâ€‹t+2â€‹x12,tâ€‹Ïƒ12â€‹(Ïƒ11+Ïƒ22)â€‹dâ€‹t+x22,tâ€‹(Ïƒ112+Ïƒ122)â€‹dâ€‹t,\displaystyle=x\_{11,t}(\sigma\_{12}^{2}+\sigma\_{22}^{2})dt+2x\_{12,t}\sigma\_{12}(\sigma\_{11}+\sigma\_{22})dt+x\_{22,t}(\sigma\_{11}^{2}+\sigma\_{12}^{2})dt, |  | (46) |
|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | dâ€‹âŸ¨x11,.,x22,.âŸ©t\displaystyle d\langle x\_{11,.},x\_{22,.}\rangle\_{t} | =4â€‹x12,tâ€‹Ïƒ12â€‹(Ïƒ11+Ïƒ22)â€‹dâ€‹t.\displaystyle=4x\_{12,t}\sigma\_{12}(\sigma\_{11}+\sigma\_{22})dt. |  | (47) |

If x11x\_{11} and x22x\_{22} represent two losses, their dependence is controlled by ([47](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S4.E47 "In 4.1 Implementation details â€£ 4 Numerical experiments â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")). Setting Ïƒ12=0\sigma\_{12}=0 results in a null instantaneous covariation. However, ([46](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S4.E46 "In 4.1 Implementation details â€£ 4 Numerical experiments â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) shows that dâ€‹âŸ¨x12,.,x12,.âŸ©tâ‰ 0d\langle x\_{12,.},x\_{12,.}\rangle\_{t}\neq 0 even if Ïƒ12=0\sigma\_{12}=0, since Ïƒâˆˆğ•Š2++\sigma\in\mathbb{S}\_{2}^{++} implies Ïƒ11>0\sigma\_{11}>0 and Ïƒ22>0\sigma\_{22}>0. The sign of this dependence is determined by the sign of Ïƒ12\sigma\_{12}, which can be positive or negative as Ïƒâˆˆğ•Š2++\sigma\in\mathbb{S}\_{2}^{++}. If Ïƒ12=0\sigma\_{12}=0, then Ïƒ2\sigma^{2} is a diagonal matrix (i.e., (Ïƒ2)12=0(\sigma^{2})\_{12}=0). Note that if we wish to change to zero the dependence between x11,tx\_{11,t} and x22,tx\_{22,t}, setting Ïƒ12=0\sigma\_{12}=0 also inadvertently lowers the quadratic variation of x11,tx\_{11,t} and x22,tx\_{22,t} (given by ([44](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S4.E44 "In 4.1 Implementation details â€£ 4 Numerical experiments â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) and ([45](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S4.E45 "In 4.1 Implementation details â€£ 4 Numerical experiments â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."))). Thus, to counteract this effect, we introduce a new matrix called Ïƒ~\tilde{\sigma} defined by

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Ïƒ~=(Ïƒ~11Ïƒ~12Ïƒ~12Ïƒ~22)=(Ïƒ112+Ïƒ12200Ïƒ222+Ïƒ122),\tilde{\sigma}=\begin{pmatrix}\tilde{\sigma}\_{11}&\tilde{\sigma}\_{12}\\ \tilde{\sigma}\_{12}&\tilde{\sigma}\_{22}\end{pmatrix}=\begin{pmatrix}\sqrt{\sigma\_{11}^{2}+\sigma\_{12}^{2}}&0\\ 0&\sqrt{\sigma\_{22}^{2}+\sigma\_{12}^{2}}\end{pmatrix}, |  | (48) |

and define a Wishart process x~t\tilde{x}\_{t} with dynamic given by ([1](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S2.E1 "In 2 The mathematical framework â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) but with Ïƒ\sigma replaced with Ïƒ~\tilde{\sigma}. We call this process the zero-dependent equivalent (to xtx\_{t}) process since, by construction, we have

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | dâ€‹âŸ¨x~11,.,x~11,.âŸ©tx~11,t\displaystyle\frac{d\langle\tilde{x}\_{11,.},\tilde{x}\_{11,.}\rangle\_{t}}{\tilde{x}\_{11,t}} | =Ïƒ112+Ïƒ122=dâ€‹âŸ¨x11,.,x11,.âŸ©tx11,t,\displaystyle=\sigma\_{11}^{2}+\sigma\_{12}^{2}=\frac{d\langle x\_{11,.},x\_{11,.}\rangle\_{t}}{x\_{11,t}}, |  | (49) |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | dâ€‹âŸ¨x~11,.,x~22,.âŸ©t\displaystyle d\langle\tilde{x}\_{11,.},\tilde{x}\_{22,.}\rangle\_{t} | =0,\displaystyle=0, |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | dâ€‹âŸ¨x~22,.,x~22,.âŸ©tx~22,t\displaystyle\frac{d\langle\tilde{x}\_{22,.},\tilde{x}\_{22,.}\rangle\_{t}}{\tilde{x}\_{22,t}} | =Ïƒ122+Ïƒ222=dâ€‹âŸ¨x22,.,x22,.âŸ©tx22,t.\displaystyle=\sigma\_{12}^{2}+\sigma\_{22}^{2}=\frac{d\langle x\_{22,.},x\_{22,.}\rangle\_{t}}{x\_{22,t}}. |  |

The process x~t\tilde{x}\_{t} allows us to quantify the impact of the dependence between x11,tx\_{11,t} and x22,tx\_{22,t} by changing the value of Ïƒ12\sigma\_{12} but keeping the quadratic variations unchanged.

In many applications, we need to find xâˆ—x\_{\*} for a given (scalar) variable XX and Î±âˆˆ]0,â€„1[\alpha\in]0,\;1[ such that ğ”¼â€‹[ğŸ{X>xâˆ—}]=Î±\mathbb{E}[\mathbf{1}\_{\{X>x\_{\*}\}}]=\alpha. In these applications, XX is defined as X=trâ€‹[Î¸â€‹xt]X=\mathrm{tr}[\theta x\_{t}] with Î¸âˆˆğ•Šn+\theta\in\mathbb{S}\_{n}^{+}, making XX a positive random variable. The Laplace transform of XX is given by â„’Xâ€‹(z)=ğ”¼â€‹[eâˆ’zâ€‹X]=Î¦â€‹(t,âˆ’zâ€‹Î¸,x0)\mathcal{L}\_{X}(z)=\mathbb{E}[e^{-zX}]=\Phi(t,-z\theta,x\_{0}) for z>0z>0, where Î¦â€‹(â‹…,â‹…,â‹…)\Phi(\cdot,\cdot,\cdot) is defined by ([4](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S2.E4 "In Proposition 2.1. â€£ 2 The mathematical framework â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")). Using the inverse Laplace transform, the cumulative distribution function of XX is:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | FXâ€‹(u)=1Ï€â€‹iâ€‹âˆ«Î³Â¯âˆ’i0Î³Â¯+iâ€‹âˆâ„œâ¡(euâ€‹zâ€‹â„’Xâ€‹(z)z)â€‹ğ‘‘z,F\_{X}(u)=\frac{1}{\pi\mathrm{i}}\int\_{\bar{\gamma}-\mathrm{i}0}^{\bar{\gamma}+\mathrm{i}\infty}\Re\left(\frac{e^{uz}\mathcal{L}\_{X}(z)}{z}\right)dz, |  |

with Î³Â¯>0\bar{\gamma}>0 and the integral computed using a quadratic integration algorithm. Since the function uâ†¦FXâ€‹(u)u\mapsto F\_{X}(u) is monotonic, the value of xâˆ—x\_{\*} such that FÂ¯Xâ€‹(xâˆ—)=1âˆ’FXâ€‹(xâˆ—)=ğ”¼â€‹[ğŸ{X>xâˆ—}]=Î±\bar{F}\_{X}(x\_{\*})=1-F\_{X}(x\_{\*})=\mathbb{E}[\mathbf{1}\_{\{X>x\_{\*}\}}]=\alpha is found iteratively.

We use the following variables to illustrate our approach. First, we consider x11,t=trâ€‹[Î¸â€‹xt]x\_{11,t}=\mathrm{tr}[\theta x\_{t}] with Î¸=e11\theta=e\_{11}, and since Î¸âˆˆğ•Š2+\theta\in\mathbb{S}\_{2}^{+} we use the Laplace/inverse Laplace transforms above to find the truncating value for the distribution of x11,tx\_{11,t}. We take xâˆ—=1.0x\_{\*}=1.0 and for which ğ”¼â€‹[ğŸ{x11,t>xâˆ—}]=0.0910\mathbb{E}[\mathbf{1}\_{\{x\_{11,t}>x\_{\*}\}}]=0.0910 when t=1t=1 and the parameters of Table [1](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.T1 "Table 1 â€£ Tables â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. As we are interested in a portfolio of losses, we consider st=x11,t+x22,t=trâ€‹[Î¸â€‹xt]s\_{t}=x\_{11,t}+x\_{22,t}=\mathrm{tr}[\theta x\_{t}] with Î¸=I2âˆˆğ•Š2++\theta=I\_{2}\in\mathbb{S}\_{2}^{++}, so that sts\_{t} is a positive random variable with a distribution that we truncate at the level sâˆ—=1.3s\_{\*}=1.3 for which ğ”¼â€‹[ğŸ{st>sâˆ—}]=0.0584\mathbb{E}[\mathbf{1}\_{\{s\_{t}>s\_{\*}\}}]=0.0584 when t=1t=1 and the parameters of Table [1](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.T1 "Table 1 â€£ Tables â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. Note that as x12,tx\_{12,t} does not need to have a positive distribution, the Laplace/inverse Laplace transform above has to be replaced by a Fourier/inverse Fourier transform but since the procedure is similar, we omit the details.

### 4.3 Effect of correlation on risk measures

We analyze the effect of changing the dependence between the losses x11,tx\_{11,t} and x22,tx\_{22,t} on different risk measures. As explained earlier, this is achieved by setting the off-diagonal term of Ïƒ\sigma to zero. We denote by x~t\tilde{x}\_{t} the zero-dependent equivalent process to xtx\_{t} and compute the different risk measures, keeping xâˆ—x\_{\*} and sâˆ—s\_{\*} unchanged. The results of the tail conditional expectation calculations are reported in TableÂ [3](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.T3 "Table 3 â€£ Tables â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.").

[ Insert TableÂ [3](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.T3 "Table 3 â€£ Tables â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.") here ]

Analyzing the effect on shortfall measures with Ïƒ\sigmaâ€™s off-diagonals set to zero reveals interesting findings. Conditioning on x11,tx\_{11,t} does not change the risk measure for both the first and second moments relative to the unchanged Ïƒ\sigma case, as expected since Ïƒ~\tilde{\sigma} satisfies ([49](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S4.E49 "In 4.1 Implementation details â€£ 4 Numerical experiments â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")). However, analyzing the sum s~t\tilde{s}\_{t} shows a decrease in shortfall compared to the correlated case, with changes of âˆ’1.71%-1.71\% and âˆ’4.84%-4.84\% for ğ”¼â€‹[s~tâ€‹âˆ£s~t>â€‹sâˆ—]\mathbb{E}[\tilde{s}\_{t}\mid\tilde{s}\_{t}>s\_{\*}] and ğ”¼â€‹[s~t2â€‹âˆ£s~t>â€‹sâˆ—]\mathbb{E}[\tilde{s}\_{t}^{2}\mid\tilde{s}\_{t}>s\_{\*}], respectively. This indicates a narrowing of the tails due to the removal of dependence between the losses. The narrowing also explains the changes observed in ğ”¼â€‹[s~tâ€‹âˆ£x~11,t>â€‹xâˆ—]\mathbb{E}[\tilde{s}\_{t}\mid\tilde{x}\_{11,t}>x\_{\*}] and ğ”¼â€‹[s~t2â€‹âˆ£x~11,t>â€‹xâˆ—]\mathbb{E}[\tilde{s}\_{t}^{2}\mid\tilde{x}\_{11,t}>x\_{\*}], with the values being âˆ’5.07%-5.07\% and âˆ’13.37%-13.37\%, respectively. Conversely, x11,tx\_{11,t} conditioned on s~t\tilde{s}\_{t} being above sâˆ—s\_{\*} increases relative to the dependent variant due to the lower expected level of s~t\tilde{s}\_{t} caused by the narrower tail. This also explains why the cross-moment x11,tâ€‹stx\_{11,t}s\_{t} conditioned on st>sâˆ—s\_{t}>s\_{\*} increases by 1.11%1.11\%. Practically, it is worth noting that higher-order moments are more affected by changes in the dependence structure between the losses. Since the dependence between losses can be difficult to measure, setting its value to zero can significantly alter risk profiles and the distribution of outcomes.

### 4.4 Two dates risk measures

We conduct numerical experiments on two different dates, t1t\_{1} and t0t\_{0} with t0<t1t\_{0}<t\_{1}, to compute the expected shortfall based on PropositionÂ [3.12](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem12 "Proposition 3.12. â€£ 3.3.1 The two dates case â€£ 3.3 Wishart conditional tail risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."). This proposition allows us to compute future expected moments conditional on past losses exceeding a certain threshold. For the dates, we take t0=1t\_{0}=1, as in the previous examples, while t1=1.5t\_{1}=1.5. The thresholds are those of the previous examples and are therefore consistent with the distribution of the process at that date. TableÂ [4](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.T4 "Table 4 â€£ Tables â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.") reports the first and second moments of x11,t1x\_{11,t\_{1}} conditional on x11,t0>xâˆ—x\_{11,t\_{0}}>x\_{\*} and similar quantities for st1s\_{t\_{1}} conditioned on st0>sâˆ—s\_{t\_{0}}>s\_{\*}, as well as the difference (in %\%) with the corresponding values of TableÂ [2](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.T2 "Table 2 â€£ Tables â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."). All the differences are negative, a result that is expected since the process reverts to its long-term mean, which is lower than its conditional expectation at earlier times. Note also that higher-order moments are more affected by this mean-reverting behavior. This modeling aspect leverages the time-dependent nature of the process and allows us to develop an intertemporal or time-lagged point of view of risk measures.

To further illustrate this feature, FigureÂ [3](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.F3 "Figure 3 â€£ Figures â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.") displays the exponential decay of the two-date expected shortfall ğ”¼â€‹[x11,t1â€‹âˆ£x11,t0>â€‹xâˆ—]\mathbb{E}[x\_{11,t\_{1}}\mid x\_{11,t\_{0}}>x\_{\*}] over the range t1âˆˆ[1,200]t\_{1}\in[1,200] to its long-term mean value of 0.840.84, with substantial decay occurring only around t=200t=200 and that is controlled by the matrix mm, in particular m11m\_{11}. This mean-reverting behavior can also be combined with a different conditioning, and to this end, the table also reports the first and second moments of x11,t1x\_{11,t\_{1}} conditioned on st0>sâˆ—s\_{t\_{0}}>s\_{\*} and similar quantities for st1s\_{t\_{1}} conditioned on x11,t0>xâˆ—x\_{11,t\_{0}}>x\_{\*}, as well as the difference (in %\%) with the corresponding values of TableÂ [2](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.T2 "Table 2 â€£ Tables â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."). All the conditional expectations are smaller than their counterparts, and of course, the mean-reverting behavior is the reason for such a result.

[ Insert TableÂ [4](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.T4 "Table 4 â€£ Tables â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.") here ]

### 4.5 Effect of dependency in capital allocation

Another use of the conditional higher moments is to solve the capital allocation problem based on the tail mean-variance model defined in Xu and Mao ([2013](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib29 "Optimal capital allocation based on the tail meanâ€“variance model")). The problem involves optimally allocating capital between losses to minimize the mean-variance of the sum of the square of the losses, conditioned on a certain level of portfolio risk. Mathematically, Theorem 2.1 of Xu and Mao ([2013](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib29 "Optimal capital allocation based on the tail meanâ€“variance model")) provides an explicit solution for a random vector of losses (Y1,â€¦,Yn)(Y\_{1},\ldots,Y\_{n}) to the allocation problem below:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | minğ©âˆˆAâ¡{ğ”¼â€‹[âˆ‘i=1n(Yiâˆ’pi)2â€‹âˆ£Z>â€‹zâˆ—]+Î³â€‹Varâ€‹(âˆ‘i=1n(Yiâˆ’pi)2â€‹âˆ£Z>â€‹zâˆ—)},\displaystyle\min\_{\mathbf{p}\in A}\left\{\mathbb{E}\left[\sum\_{i=1}^{n}(Y\_{i}-p\_{i})^{2}\mid Z>z\_{\*}\right]+\gamma\text{Var}\left(\sum\_{i=1}^{n}(Y\_{i}-p\_{i})^{2}\mid Z>z\_{\*}\right)\right\}, |  | (50) |

where A={ğ©âˆˆâ„n:p1+â€¦+pn=c}A=\{\mathbf{p}\in\mathbb{R}^{n}:p\_{1}+\ldots+p\_{n}=c\} with the allocation budget c>0c>0, Î³>0\gamma>0, and ZZ is the conditioning variable and zâˆ—z\_{\*} a given threshold. The above conditional expectations can be reformulated in our framework using Remark [3.6](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem6 "Remark 3.6. â€£ 3.2 One-dimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."). Xu and Mao ([2013](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib29 "Optimal capital allocation based on the tail meanâ€“variance model")) illustrate their results using the multivariate elliptical distribution. Li and Yin ([2024](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib28 "The tail meanâ€“variance optimal capital allocation under the extended skew-elliptical distribution")) analyze the same model using the skew-elliptical distribution but underline the difficulty of the problem. Indeed, they state, â€œâ€¦ the computational challenge arises due to the calculation involving conditional joint moments of underlying risksâ€ (see Li and Yin ([2024](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib28 "The tail meanâ€“variance optimal capital allocation under the extended skew-elliptical distribution"), p. 2)). Yang et al. ([2025](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib27 "Tail moments and tail joint moments for multivariate generalized hyperbolic distribution")) solve the same problem for the multivariate generalized hyperbolic distribution. One of the difficulties with this model is that it necessitates the computation of ğ”¼â€‹[Yj2â€‹Yiâ€‹|Z>â€‹zâˆ—]\mathbb{E}[Y\_{j}^{2}Y\_{i}|Z>z\_{\*}] and ğ”¼â€‹[Yjâ€‹Yiâ€‹|Z>â€‹zâˆ—]\mathbb{E}[Y\_{j}Y\_{i}|Z>z\_{\*}] for j,i=1,â€¦,nj,i=1,\ldots,n. Thanks to the strong analytical properties of our results, this difficulty is easily handled in our framework. Note that ğ”¼â€‹[Yjâ€‹Yiâ€‹|Z>â€‹zâˆ—]\mathbb{E}[Y\_{j}Y\_{i}|Z>z\_{\*}] is the first term of TCovY1,Y2|Zâ¡(zâˆ—)\operatorname{TCov}\_{Y\_{1},Y\_{2}|Z}(z\_{\*}) of ([42](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E42 "In The Tail covariance (TCov): â€£ 3.5 Conditional higher moments tail risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."))  while ğ”¼â€‹[Yj2â€‹Yiâ€‹|Z>â€‹zâˆ—]\mathbb{E}[Y\_{j}^{2}Y\_{i}|Z>z\_{\*}] is a third-order conditional moment.

Note that the original result of Xu and Mao ([2013](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib29 "Optimal capital allocation based on the tail meanâ€“variance model")) is based on conditioning on the sum of the random variables YiY\_{i} (i.e., setting ZZ to be S=âˆ‘i=1nYiS=\sum\_{i=1}^{n}Y\_{i} with S>VaRqâ€‹(S)S>\text{VaR}\_{q}(S), the conditioning of the sum on the value-at-risk). However, the proof of their result does not require this specific condition, and thus we can choose ZZ to be another variable or combination of variables. Since this problem heavily relies on the dependence between the losses, the conditioning is performed on the variable x12,tx\_{12,t}, thereby quantifying the impact of loss dependence on the capital allocation. It exploits the matrix nature of the Wishart process for modeling risk measures. It will demonstrate the importance of appropriately accounting for dependency in risk management within the Wishart process. To this end, we proceed as above, solving the problem using the parameters of TableÂ [1](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.T1 "Table 1 â€£ Tables â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.") and then considering the process x~t\tilde{x}\_{t}, the zero-dependent equivalent process to xtx\_{t}, and solving the problem ([50](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S4.E50 "In 4.5 Effect of dependency in capital allocation â€£ 4 Numerical experiments â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")). A comparison between the two solutions illustrates the impact of the lossesâ€™ dependence on the capital allocation.

First, we consider the capital allocation problem with Wishart parameters in TableÂ [1](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.T1 "Table 1 â€£ Tables â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."), time value of t=1t=1, the allocation budget c=1.3c=1.3, Î³=1\gamma=1, and set the conditioning random variable to be x12,t>VaR0.95â€‹(trâ€‹[Î¸â€‹xt])x\_{12,t}>\text{VaR}\_{0.95}(\text{tr}[\theta x\_{t}]), where Î¸=(e12+e21)/2\theta=(e\_{12}+e\_{21})/2. Note that the values of VaR0.95â€‹(trâ€‹[Î¸â€‹xt])\text{VaR}\_{0.95}(\text{tr}[\theta x\_{t}]) and VaR0.95â€‹(trâ€‹[Î¸â€‹x~t])\text{VaR}\_{0.95}(\text{tr}[\theta\tilde{x}\_{t}]) are different to account for the difference in the quadratic variations between x11,tx\_{11,t} and x22,tx\_{22,t} and between x~11,t\tilde{x}\_{11,t} and x~22,t\tilde{x}\_{22,t}. In particular, for the dependent case, we have VaR0.95â€‹(trâ€‹[Î¸â€‹xt])=0.438\text{VaR}\_{0.95}(\text{tr}[\theta x\_{t}])=0.438, while in the diagonal case Ïƒ~\tilde{\sigma} given by ([48](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S4.E48 "In 4.1 Implementation details â€£ 4 Numerical experiments â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) we have VaR0.95â€‹(trâ€‹[Î¸â€‹x~t])=0.085\text{VaR}\_{0.95}(\text{tr}[\theta\tilde{x}\_{t}])=0.085.

The optimal allocation values for ([50](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S4.E50 "In 4.5 Effect of dependency in capital allocation â€£ 4 Numerical experiments â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) for the case in TableÂ [1](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.T1 "Table 1 â€£ Tables â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.") are p1=1.031p\_{1}=1.031 and p2=0.269p\_{2}=0.269, which gives a ratio of p1/p2=3.836p\_{1}/p\_{2}=3.836. In comparison, when using x~t\tilde{x}\_{t}, the optimal allocation is p~1=0.965\tilde{p}\_{1}=0.965 and p~2=0.335\tilde{p}\_{2}=0.335, with a ratio of p~1/p~2=2.877\tilde{p}\_{1}/\tilde{p}\_{2}=2.877. The difference in the allocations is best viewed through their ratios, and the impact of the dependence on this ratio is substantial. Having a dependency between the losses suggests allocating more to the loss with more variance (in this case, x11,tx\_{11,t}). Thus, an erroneous assumption of independence or a significant error in its estimation can lead to a situation where one loss is under-capitalized and another over-capitalized.

As previously demonstrated, the Wishart process is highly tractable and is a natural framework to model dependent losses since it is, by construction, a positive definite matrix process. Furthermore, due to its tractability, we are even able to derive allocation results, and the results highlight that if dependence is not appropriately accounted for, it can lead to incorrect allocation of resources.

### 4.6 Empirical estimation

Practical applicability is an important criterion when evaluating the usefulness of a model. We illustrate our approach using the Danish Fire Loss dataset, a standard benchmark in insurance. The raw data contain 2,167 fire insurance claims from 1980 to 1990, measured in millions of DKK.999Note that we do not apply a logarithmic transformation, as in Ignatieva and Landsman ([2021](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib43 "A class of generalised hyper-elliptical distributions and their applications in computing conditional tail risk measures")). We focus on the *Building* and *Contents* lines, excluding *Profit* due to the many zeros, and we aggregate claim amounts to weekly totals, retaining weeks with strictly positive totals in both lines. Throughout, we treat these weekly bivariate observations as i.i.d. draws rather than a time series. As a result, for the model we estimate the parameters of its limiting, stationary distribution. By CorollaryÂ [2.2](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S2.Thmtheorem2 "Corollary 2.2. â€£ 2 The mathematical framework â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."), this distribution is matrix gamma with scale 2â€‹Ï‚âˆ2\varsigma\_{\infty} and shape Î²/2\beta/2. The pair (Î²,Ï‚âˆ)(\beta,\varsigma\_{\infty}) is obtained by the method of moments, as in GouriÃ©roux et al. ([2009](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib32 "The Wishart autoregressive process of multivariate stochastic volatility")) or GouriÃ©roux and Lu ([2025](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib2 "Partial observability of implied volatility matrices: Identification and covolatilities filtering"), PropositionÂ 2), and the explicit equations are given in the supplementary appendix. In other words, we fit the stationary law to the weekly aggregates, then compute the risk measures developed in this paper from the fitted law.

If only the diagonal terms of the process are used to estimate the parameters, then only Ï‚iâ€‹j,âˆ2\varsigma\_{ij,\infty}^{2} can be identified; see the supplementary appendix for the expressions of the estimators. Since we have ğ”¼â€‹[xiâ€‹j,âˆ]=Î²â€‹Ï‚iâ€‹j,âˆ\mathbb{E}[x\_{ij,\infty}]=\beta\varsigma\_{ij,\infty}, this suggests specifying the sign of Ï‚iâ€‹j,âˆ\varsigma\_{ij,\infty} using the sign of the correlation between xiâ€‹i,âˆx\_{ii,\infty} and xjâ€‹j,âˆx\_{jj,\infty}. These estimators yield the model parameters reported in TableÂ [5](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.T5 "Table 5 â€£ Tables â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.").

[ Insert TableÂ [5](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.T5 "Table 5 â€£ Tables â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.") here ]

The implied correlation from the fitted matrix gamma distribution is 0.44, and is close to the sample correlation of 0.56 from the weekly aggregates, which indicates a reasonable fit. Using PropositionÂ [3.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem1 "Proposition 3.1. â€£ 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."), we compute the model implied risk measures, see TableÂ [6](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.T6 "Table 6 â€£ Tables â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."). For reference, we also report the empirical, nonparametric counterparts computed directly from the weekly data. The model implied quantities track their empirical analogues closely, which supports the adequacy of the limiting distribution specification for this application.

[ Insert TableÂ [6](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.T6 "Table 6 â€£ Tables â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.") here ]

## 5 Conclusion

In this work, we introduce an analytical framework capable of quantifying multivariate risk measures while incorporating temporal aspects. The flexibility of the framework lies in its reliance solely on the characteristic function. We present Fourier transforms of tail conditional moments and their cross-moments, and show that this approach reduces a two-dimensional integration problem to a one-dimensional one. We compute the tail conditional expectation for various cross-moments, both at a single point in time and across multiple time points. This flexible framework is demonstrated using the Wishart processâ€”a highly tractable matrix affine process characterized by its positive definitenessâ€”making it well-suited for loss modeling. We provide a numerical implementation of the derived framework and demonstrate the impact of dependency between loss items. Our results show that removing dependency can lead to significant differences in the tail conditional expectation, with variations of up to 13.37% at a fixed point in time and up to 18.86% across time. We further demonstrate that our method and model can be applied in the context of capital allocation, showcasing that we are able to obtain operational results for the model proposed by Xu and Mao ([2013](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib29 "Optimal capital allocation based on the tail meanâ€“variance model")). Overall, our framework offers a robust and flexible tool for risk management, capable of handling complex dependencies and temporal evolutions in multivariate loss processes.

|  | Risk measureValueDiff.%ğ”¼â€‹[x11,t1â€‹âˆ£x11,t0>â€‹xâˆ—]1.0405âˆ’2.00ğ”¼â€‹[x11,t12â€‹âˆ£x11,t0>â€‹xâˆ—]1.0944âˆ’3.19ğ”¼â€‹[st1â€‹âˆ£st0>â€‹sâˆ—]1.3406âˆ’2.41ğ”¼â€‹[st12â€‹âˆ£st0>â€‹sâˆ—]1.8160âˆ’4.03ğ”¼â€‹[x11,tâ€‹|st>â€‹sâˆ—]1.0594âˆ’1.97ğ”¼â€‹[x11,t2â€‹|st>â€‹sâˆ—]1.1346âˆ’3.14ğ”¼â€‹[stâ€‹|x11,t>â€‹xâˆ—]1.3011âˆ’2.32ğ”¼â€‹[st2â€‹|x11,t>â€‹xâˆ—]1.7127âˆ’3.80\begin{array}[]{lcc}\textrm{Risk measure}&\textrm{Value}&\textrm{Diff.}\%\\ \hline\cr\mathbb{E}\left[x\_{11,t\_{1}}\mid x\_{11,\,t\_{0}}>x\_{\*}\right]&1.0405&-2.00\\ \mathbb{E}\left[x\_{11,t\_{1}}^{2}\mid x\_{11,\,t\_{0}}>x\_{\*}\right]&1.0944&-3.19\\ \mathbb{E}\left[s\_{t\_{1}}\mid s\_{t\_{0}}>s\_{\*}\right]&1.3406&-2.41\\ \mathbb{E}\left[s\_{t\_{1}}^{2}\mid s\_{t\_{0}}>s\_{\*}\right]&1.8160&-4.03\\ \mathbb{E}\left[x\_{11,t}|s\_{t}>s\_{\*}\right]&1.0594&-1.97\\ \mathbb{E}\left[x\_{11,t}^{2}|s\_{t}>s\_{\*}\right]&1.1346&-3.14\\ \mathbb{E}\left[s\_{t}|x\_{11,t}>x\_{\*}\right]&1.3011&-2.32\\ \mathbb{E}\left[s\_{t}^{2}|x\_{11,t}>x\_{\*}\right]&1.7127&-3.80\\ \hline\cr\end{array} |  |

Online supplementary materials to:

Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach

by

JosÃ© Da Fonseca and Patrick Wong

##### A comparison with Ignatieva and Landsman ([2019](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib42 "Conditional tail risk measures for the skewed generalised hyperbolic family")) and Ignatieva and Landsman ([2025](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib44 "Tail variance for generalised hyper-elliptical models")):

We provide complete details, using the methodology presented in this paper, on the implementation of the expected shortfall, the tail variance and the tail skewness for a univariate random variable following a Generalised Hyperbolic (GH) distribution. For the expected shortfall, it is given by ([36](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E36 "In 3.4 A note on numerical precision â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) and corresponds to Ignatieva and Landsman ([2019](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib42 "Conditional tail risk measures for the skewed generalised hyperbolic family"), Eq. (3.4)). As in Ignatieva and Landsman ([2019](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib42 "Conditional tail risk measures for the skewed generalised hyperbolic family")), we derive the expression for the characteristic function of the univariate GH distribution from the moment generating function ([35](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E35 "In 3.4 A note on numerical precision â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")), and it corresponds to Ignatieva and Landsman ([2019](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib42 "Conditional tail risk measures for the skewed generalised hyperbolic family"), Eq.Â (2.6)), where we correct for a missing square root in the modified Bessel function of the third kind that appears in the denominator. Following Ignatieva and Landsman ([2019](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib42 "Conditional tail risk measures for the skewed generalised hyperbolic family")), see Paolella ([2007](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib38 "Intermediate probability: a computational approach")) for further details.

Given a scalar variable Yâˆ¼Gâ€‹H1â€‹(Î»,Ï‡,Ïˆ,Î¼,Ïƒ2,Î³)Y\sim GH\_{1}(\lambda,\chi,\psi,\mu,\sigma^{2},\gamma) with Î»,Ï‡,Ïˆ,Î¼,Ïƒ2,Î³\lambda,\chi,\psi,\mu,\sigma^{2},\gamma scalar values and Ï‡>0\chi>0 and Ïˆ>0\psi>0, the univariate GH distribution with density ([38](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E38 "In 3.4 A note on numerical precision â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")). Then the moment generating function of YY, given by ([35](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E35 "In 3.4 A note on numerical precision â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")), is of scalar argument and simplifies to

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Î¦Yâ€‹(v)=evâ€‹Î¼â€‹(ÏˆÏˆâˆ’2â€‹vâ€‹Î³âˆ’v2â€‹Ïƒ2)Î»/2â€‹KÎ»â€‹(Ï‡â€‹(Ïˆâˆ’2â€‹vâ€‹Î³âˆ’v2â€‹Ïƒ2))KÎ»â€‹(Ï‡â€‹Ïˆ).\displaystyle\Phi\_{Y}(v)=e^{v\mu}\left(\frac{\psi}{\psi-2v\gamma-v^{2}\sigma^{2}}\right)^{\lambda/2}\frac{K\_{\lambda}\left(\sqrt{\chi\left(\psi-2v\gamma-v^{2}\sigma^{2}\right)}\right)}{K\_{\lambda}\left(\sqrt{\chi\psi}\right)}. |  | (51) |

The tail conditional expectation TCEYâ¡(yâˆ—)\operatorname{TCE}\_{Y}(y\_{\*}) is equal to ([19](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E19 "In 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) with p=1p=1, that is

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ğ”¼â€‹[Yâ€‹|Y>â€‹yâˆ—]=ğ”¼â€‹[Yâ€‹ğŸ{Y>yâˆ—}]ğ”¼â€‹[ğŸ{Y>yâˆ—}],\displaystyle\mathbb{E}[Y|Y>y\_{\*}]=\frac{\mathbb{E}[Y\mathbf{1}\_{\{Y>y\_{\*}\}}]}{\mathbb{E}[\mathbf{1}\_{\{Y>y\_{\*}\}}]}, |  | (52) |

and according to Proposition [3.1](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.Thmtheorem1 "Proposition 3.1. â€£ 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies."), the expectation in the numerator is given by

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ğ”¼â€‹[Yâ€‹ğŸ{Y>yâˆ—}]=1Ï€â€‹âˆ«0+âˆâ„œâ¡((yâˆ—(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)+1(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)2)â€‹eâˆ’(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)â€‹yâˆ—â€‹Î¦Yâ€‹(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1))â€‹ğ‘‘u1,\displaystyle\mathbb{E}[Y\mathbf{1}\_{\{Y>y\_{\*}\}}]=\frac{1}{\pi}\int\_{0}^{+\infty}\Re\left(\left(\frac{y\_{\*}}{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})}+\frac{1}{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})^{2}}\right)e^{-(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})y\_{\*}}\Phi\_{Y}(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})\right)du\_{1}, |  | (53) |

while the denominator is

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ğ”¼â€‹[ğŸ{Y>yâˆ—}]=1Ï€â€‹âˆ«0+âˆâ„œâ¡(eâˆ’(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)â€‹yâˆ—â€‹Î¦Yâ€‹(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1))â€‹ğ‘‘u1.\displaystyle\mathbb{E}[\mathbf{1}\_{\{Y>y\_{\*}\}}]=\frac{1}{\pi}\int\_{0}^{+\infty}\Re\left(\frac{e^{-(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})y\_{\*}}\Phi\_{Y}(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})}{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})}\right)du\_{1}. |  | (54) |

It remains to check the integrability of these functions. The second integrand in ([53](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.E53 "In A comparison with Ignatieva and Landsman (2019) and Ignatieva and Landsman (2025): â€£ Figures â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) leads to

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | |âˆ«0+âˆâ„œâ¡(eâˆ’(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)â€‹yâˆ—â€‹Î¦Yâ€‹(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)2)â€‹ğ‘‘u1|â‰¤câ€‹âˆ«0+âˆ|Î¦Yâ€‹(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)||(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)2|â€‹ğ‘‘u1,\displaystyle\left|\int\_{0}^{+\infty}\Re\left(\frac{e^{-(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})y\_{\*}}\Phi\_{Y}(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})}{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})^{2}}\right)du\_{1}\right|\leq c\int\_{0}^{+\infty}\frac{|\Phi\_{Y}(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})|}{|(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})^{2}|}du\_{1}, |  | (55) |

with c>0c>0 and as |Î¦Yâ€‹(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)|â‰¤|ğ”¼â€‹[e(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)â€‹Y]|â‰¤|ğ”¼â€‹[eÎ±1â€‹Y]||\Phi\_{Y}(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})|\leq|\mathbb{E}[e^{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})Y}]|\leq|\mathbb{E}[e^{\alpha\_{1}Y}]| is finite for Î±1\alpha\_{1} sufficiently small since Ïˆ>0\psi>0, we conclude the integral is well defined. Note that Î±1\alpha\_{1} can have any sign. The integral ([54](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.E54 "In A comparison with Ignatieva and Landsman (2019) and Ignatieva and Landsman (2025): â€£ Figures â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) and the first integrand of ([53](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.E53 "In A comparison with Ignatieva and Landsman (2019) and Ignatieva and Landsman (2025): â€£ Figures â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) are also well defined since we have

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | |âˆ«0+âˆâ„œâ¡(eâˆ’(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)â€‹yâˆ—â€‹Î¦Yâ€‹(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1))â€‹ğ‘‘u1|â‰¤câ€‹âˆ«0+âˆ|Î¦Yâ€‹(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)||(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)|â€‹ğ‘‘u1,\displaystyle\left|\int\_{0}^{+\infty}\Re\left(\frac{e^{-(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})y\_{\*}}\Phi\_{Y}(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})}{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})}\right)du\_{1}\right|\leq c\int\_{0}^{+\infty}\frac{|\Phi\_{Y}(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})|}{|(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})|}du\_{1}, |  | (56) |

with c>0c>0 (a generic constant that may change from one equation to the other), and using DLMF ([2010](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib45 "Digital library of mathematical functions"), (10.25.3)) we have for u1u\_{1} large (and positive)

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | |Î¦Yâ€‹(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)|â‰¤câ€‹eâˆ’Ï‡â€‹(Ïˆâˆ’2â€‹Î±1â€‹Î³+u12â€‹Ïƒ2)+iâ€‹Ï‡â€‹(2â€‹u1â€‹Î³+2â€‹Î±1â€‹u1â€‹Ïƒ2)|(Ïˆâˆ’2â€‹Î±1â€‹Î³+u12â€‹Ïƒ2)+iâ€‹(2â€‹u1â€‹Î³+2â€‹Î±1â€‹u1â€‹Ïƒ2)|Î»/2+1/4,\displaystyle|\Phi\_{Y}(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})|\leq c\frac{e^{-\sqrt{\chi(\psi-2\alpha\_{1}\gamma+u\_{1}^{2}\sigma^{2})+\mathrm{i}\chi(2u\_{1}\gamma+2\alpha\_{1}u\_{1}\sigma^{2})}}}{|(\psi-2\alpha\_{1}\gamma+u\_{1}^{2}\sigma^{2})+\mathrm{i}(2u\_{1}\gamma+2\alpha\_{1}u\_{1}\sigma^{2})|^{\lambda/2+1/4}}, |  | (57) |

with c>0c>0. For u1u\_{1} large we get, since Ï‡>0\chi>0, that there exists c>0c>0 such that

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | |Î¦Yâ€‹(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)|â‰¤câ€‹eâˆ’Ï‡â€‹u1â€‹Ïƒu1Î»+1/2,\displaystyle|\Phi\_{Y}(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})|\leq c\frac{e^{-\sqrt{\chi}u\_{1}\sigma}}{u\_{1}^{\lambda+1/2}}, |  | (58) |

and this upper bound combined with ([56](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.E56 "In A comparison with Ignatieva and Landsman (2019) and Ignatieva and Landsman (2025): â€£ Figures â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) implies the integral is well defined. As result, ([53](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.E53 "In A comparison with Ignatieva and Landsman (2019) and Ignatieva and Landsman (2025): â€£ Figures â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) and ([54](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.E54 "In A comparison with Ignatieva and Landsman (2019) and Ignatieva and Landsman (2025): â€£ Figures â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) are well defined and therefore the expected shortfall ([52](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.E52 "In A comparison with Ignatieva and Landsman (2019) and Ignatieva and Landsman (2025): â€£ Figures â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) is also well defined.

For the tail variance, when p=2p=2 in ([19](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E19 "In 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) leads to

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ğ”¼â€‹[Y2â€‹ğŸ{Y>yâˆ—}]=1Ï€â€‹âˆ«0+âˆâ„œâ¡((yâˆ—2(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)+2â€‹yâˆ—(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)2+2(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)3)â€‹eâˆ’(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)â€‹yâˆ—â€‹Î¦Yâ€‹(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1))â€‹ğ‘‘u1,\displaystyle\mathbb{E}[Y^{2}\mathbf{1}\_{\{Y>y\_{\*}\}}]=\frac{1}{\pi}\int\_{0}^{+\infty}\Re\left(\left(\frac{y\_{\*}^{2}}{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})}+\frac{2y\_{\*}}{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})^{2}}+\frac{2}{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})^{3}}\right)e^{-(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})y\_{\*}}\Phi\_{Y}(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})\right)du\_{1}, |  | (59) |

and, as previously mentioned, the TVYâ¡(yâˆ—)\operatorname{TV}\_{Y}(y\_{\*}) of ([40](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E40 "In The Tail variance (TV): â€£ 3.5 Conditional higher moments tail risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) is known and given by

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | TVYâ¡(yâˆ—)=ğ”¼â€‹[Y2â€‹âˆ£Y>â€‹yâˆ—]ğ”¼â€‹[ğŸ{Y>yâˆ—}]âˆ’(ğ”¼â€‹[Yâ€‹âˆ£Y>â€‹yâˆ—])2.\displaystyle\operatorname{TV}\_{Y}(y\_{\*})=\frac{\mathbb{E}[Y^{2}\mid Y>y\_{\*}]}{\mathbb{E}[\mathbf{1}\_{\{Y>y\_{\*}\}}]}-(\mathbb{E}[Y\mid Y>y\_{\*}])^{2}. |  | (60) |

The integral above can be decomposed as a sum of three integrals, the first two being well defined according to the verifications already done, and the last one is also well defined. As a result, the tail variance risk representation based on the MGF is well defined.

In Ignatieva and Landsman ([2025](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib44 "Tail variance for generalised hyper-elliptical models")), the following explicit expression is derived for the tail variance risk measure when Yâˆ¼Gâ€‹H1â€‹(Î»,Ï‡,Ïˆ,Î¼,Ïƒ2,Î³)Y\sim GH\_{1}(\lambda,\chi,\psi,\mu,\sigma^{2},\gamma):

|  |  |  |  |

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | +k~Î»â€‹Î³1âˆ’qâ€‹FÂ¯GH1â€‹(yâˆ—;Î»+2,Ï‡,Ïˆ,Î¼,Ïƒ2,Î³)â€‹(Î³+Ïƒ2â€‹fGH1â€‹(yâˆ—;Î»+2,Ï‡,Ïˆ,Î¼,Ïƒ2,Î³)FÂ¯GH1â€‹(yâˆ—;Î»+2,Ï‡,Ïˆ,Î¼,Ïƒ2,Î³))\displaystyle+\frac{\tilde{k}\_{\lambda}\gamma}{1-q}\bar{F}\_{\mathrm{GH}\_{1}}(y\_{\*};\lambda+2,\chi,\psi,\mu,\sigma^{2},\gamma)\left(\gamma+\sigma^{2}\frac{f\_{\mathrm{GH}\_{1}}(y\_{\*};\lambda+2,\chi,\psi,\mu,\sigma^{2},\gamma)}{\bar{F}\_{\mathrm{GH}\_{1}}(y\_{\*};\lambda+2,\chi,\psi,\mu,\sigma^{2},\gamma)}\right) |  |

###### Remark .1.

Note that there is a typo in Ignatieva and Landsman ([2025](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib44 "Tail variance for generalised hyper-elliptical models"), Eq.Â (3.6)). In the second line of this equation, the term FÂ¯GH1â€‹(xq;Î¼,Ïƒ2,g,Î³,l,Î»~2,Ï‡,Ïˆ)\bar{F}\_{\mathrm{GH}\_{1}}(x\_{q};\mu,\sigma^{2},g,\gamma,l,\tilde{\lambda}\_{2},\chi,\psi) should be replaced by FÂ¯GH1â€‹(xq;Î¼,Ïƒ2,g,Î³,l,Î»~4,Ï‡,Ïˆ)\bar{F}\_{\mathrm{GH}\_{1}}(x\_{q};\mu,\sigma^{2},g,\gamma,l,\tilde{\lambda}\_{4},\chi,\psi) (in the notations of Ignatieva and Landsman ([2025](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib44 "Tail variance for generalised hyper-elliptical models"))).

Of course, ([60](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.E60 "In A comparison with Ignatieva and Landsman (2019) and Ignatieva and Landsman (2025): â€£ Figures â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) computed using the MGF and ([61](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.E61 "In A comparison with Ignatieva and Landsman (2019) and Ignatieva and Landsman (2025): â€£ Figures â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) should yield the same numerical results.

Lastly, for the tail skewness, when p=3p=3 in ([19](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E19 "In 3.1 Multidimensional Fourier transform representations for risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")), the simplicity of the method proposed in our work allows us to compute

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ğ”¼â€‹[Y3â€‹ğŸ{Y>yâˆ—}]\displaystyle\mathbb{E}[Y^{3}\mathbf{1}\_{\{Y>y\_{\*}\}}] | =1Ï€â€‹âˆ«0+âˆâ„œâ¡((yâˆ—3(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)+3â€‹yâˆ—2(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)2+6â€‹yâˆ—(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)3)â€‹eâˆ’(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)â€‹yâˆ—â€‹Î¦Yâ€‹(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1))â€‹ğ‘‘u1\displaystyle=\frac{1}{\pi}\int\_{0}^{+\infty}\Re\left(\left(\frac{y\_{\*}^{3}}{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})}+\frac{3y\_{\*}^{2}}{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})^{2}}+\frac{6y\_{\*}}{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})^{3}}\right)e^{-(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})y\_{\*}}\Phi\_{Y}(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})\right)du\_{1} |  |
|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | +1Ï€â€‹âˆ«0+âˆâ„œâ¡(6(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)4â€‹eâˆ’(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1)â€‹yâˆ—â€‹Î¦Yâ€‹(Î±1âˆ’iâ€‹u1))â€‹ğ‘‘u1,\displaystyle+\frac{1}{\pi}\int\_{0}^{+\infty}\Re\left(\frac{6}{(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})^{4}}e^{-(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})y\_{\*}}\Phi\_{Y}(\alpha\_{1}-\mathrm{i}u\_{1})\right)du\_{1}, |  | (62) |

with the first integral above being well-defined, since ([59](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.E59 "In A comparison with Ignatieva and Landsman (2019) and Ignatieva and Landsman (2025): â€£ Figures â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) is, while the last integral is also well-defined. Combining this expectation with the tail conditional variance ([60](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.E60 "In A comparison with Ignatieva and Landsman (2019) and Ignatieva and Landsman (2025): â€£ Figures â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) and the expression ([43](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#S3.E43 "In The Tail skewness (TS): â€£ 3.5 Conditional higher moments tail risk measures â€£ 3 Conditional tail risk measures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks. We also thank the participants at CICIRM 2024, Ningbo, China and IME 2024, Chicago, USA, for their remarks. The usual caveat applies.")) gives us the tail skewness, which is yet to be computed in the case of Ignatieva and Landsman ([2025](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib44 "Tail variance for generalised hyper-elliptical models")).

Let us verify that the tail conditional expectation and tail variance values obtained using the approach based on the MGF match those reported by Ignatieva and Landsman ([2019](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib42 "Conditional tail risk measures for the skewed generalised hyperbolic family")) and Ignatieva and Landsman ([2025](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib44 "Tail variance for generalised hyper-elliptical models")). For the tail skewness, we provide its value, which could be used to validate a formula based on the density once such a formula becomes available.

(or Ignatieva and Landsman ([2025](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#bib.bib44 "Tail variance for generalised hyper-elliptical models"), Eq.Â (3.6))), as well as using the moment generating function ([52](https://arxiv.org/html/2602.06401v1#Ax1.E52 "In A comparison with Ignatieva and Landsman (2019) and Ignatieva and Landsman (2025): â€£ Figures â€£ Tables and figures â€£ Wishart conditional tail risk measures: An analytic approach1footnote 11footnote 1We thank Katja Ignatieva for her useful suggestions and remarks.
